Her first husband: as for the absent one divorced for lack of maintenance, Abd al-Baqi said in his commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil: the woman divorced for lack of maintenance marries and he consummates, then her dropping appears [؟] the divorcer by establishing evidence that he used to send it to her and that she received it or that he left it with her, so the entry of the second does not separate her. And as for the one whose husband is claimed [dead?], Abd al-Baqi also said: if she is informed by other than two trustworthy witnesses of his death, and she relies, observes the waiting period, and marries, then he [the first husband] arrives, he [the first] does not lose her by the entry of the second, even if she gives birth to children from him, whether the judge ruled or not, according to the well-known view. And she is returned to him in both cases without a new contract or dowry, and she must observe istibra' with three menses if she menstruates, or with a pregnancy if pregnant, or three months if she is young or menopausal. The full dower prescribed, or if not, the dower of the like, is due from the second for the intercourse, even if it is forbidden. Al-Dardir said: the full prescribed dower and the dower of the like in case of delegation due to intercourse with a divorced woman of age, even if that intercourse is forbidden, and the lineage of the children is attributed to the second. And there is no disagreement on this in the Maliki school. As for the fourth question, al-Dardir said: the decree of divorce from the missing husband until the beginning of the waiting period separates her; it is realized by the entry of the second husband upon her, so that if the first came before the entry of the second, he is more entitled to her, and after the entry she becomes separated from the first and takes from him all the dower if he had not consummated, so it does not apply except to the wife of the missing. As for the insolvent and the one divorced for lack of maintenance, the entry of the second does not separate her, even if she gives birth to children from him, as mentioned in the third question. And if he secludes with her a valid seclusion, he has consummated. And in the gloss of al-Adawi on the collection of al-Amir at his statement: 'and the decree of divorce is realized upon the entry of the second' meaning his seclusion with her if he denies pleasure, because seclusion is a presumption and stands in its place, as in al-Tawdih. As for the fifth question, the answer: the matters in which the general body of Muslims acts in place of the judge are many, including the case of the missing. His wife must choose one of two: either she is content to remain with her missing husband, or she wants separation. If she wants it, she must raise her case to the judge or the ruler or the officer [؟] and if there is none, then to the general body of Muslims from the righteous of her town and neighbors. And as for her observing the waiting period and marrying another man without raising her case to the judge and those mentioned, no one says it is permissible or lawful due to the corruption in it. As for the sixth question, the answer: the cases that are referred to the general body of Muslims must be in accordance with their madhhab, because talfiq is forbidden by consensus. And Allah Almighty knows best. It was written by Muhammad al-Tayyib ibn Ishaq al-Ansari al-Madani, servant of knowledge in the al-Badri mosque. The answer from the scholar al-Salih al-Tunisi al-Maliki, teacher at the eastern mosque in Medina. In the name of Allah, etc. After praise, a question derived from the case of the missing reached me, and it is this.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Maliki legal responses concerning the wife of a missing husband (mafqud) or a husband unable to provide maintenance. The rulings are extracted from Maliki authorities: Abd al-Baqi's commentary on Khalil and al-Dardir's work. The author presents these to show the Maliki position on key issues: when a second marriage invalidates the first, conditions for validity, and the prohibition of talfiq. The passage concludes with a critical rule for muftis: wherever a ruling is referred to the general body of Muslims (jama'ah al-muslimin), it must conform to their madhhab, because talfiq (mixing rulings from different schools) is haram by consensus. This is a rasm al-mufti principle: do not issue fatwas by combining doctrines from different madhhabs in a way that leads to talfiq. The Hanafi school holds the same position on the prohibition of talfiq. For the specific issues of the missing husband, the Hanafi rulings may differ; this text only presents the Maliki view.

Key Terms
التلفيق (al-talfiq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs in a single action or fatwa without following a consistent school
المفقود (al-mafqud): A husband who is missing and whose whereabouts and life status are unknown

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They may issue any ruling as long as it does not harm the woman.
D) They must refer the case to a Maliki scholar.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is haram by consensus; a mufti must ensure his fatwa adheres to a single madhhab consistently.

Talfiq and Council Authority in Mixed-Madhhab Divorce Cases
Fatwa response and further questions on talfiq and council authority in mixed-madhhab divorce cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'qada al-qadi idha sara mahallan mujtahadan fihi nafadh' to a mixed-madhhab fatwa scenario and identify when talfiq is permissible across separate issues.

Core Idea
A council ruling on a matter of ijtihad is enforceable; talfiq across separate issues is permitted.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah presents a real fatwa exchange between Maliki and Hanafi scholars. The core legal issue is whether a Hanafi council can grant a divorce based on grounds not recognized by Malikis, and whether that constitutes impermissible talfiq. Understanding this requires mastery of two key principles: the enforceability of ijtihad-based rulings and the boundaries of talfiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal issues involved
Distinguish the council's authority to act as a judge (one issue) from the specific ground for separation (another issue). This is crucial for the talfiq analysis.
The Hanafi response argues these are separate issues, so talfiq is permissible.
2
Apply the principle of qada al-qadi
The maxim 'qada al-qadi idha sara mahallan mujtahadan fihi nafadh' states that a judge's ruling in a matter of ijtihad is enforceable. The council (jamā'a) takes the place of a judge.
The ruling in question is a matter of ijtihad because schools differ on musahara as a ground for divorce.
3
Analyze the talfiq objection
Maliki scholars object that the Hanafi council's ruling is talfiq within a single issue. The response distinguishes two separate issues, making talfiq permissible.
Talfiq within one issue is prohibited, but across multiple issues it is allowed.
4
Determine the practical outcome
The Hanafi council's ruling for separation is enforceable even according to Malikis, because it is a matter of ijtihad and the council acts as a judge.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the ruling is valid and binding.
5
Apply to the third question on continuous insanity
The same principles apply: the council can follow its own madhhab's conditions (immediate separation) rather than Maliki's one-year wait, because it is a matter of ijtihad.
The council must rule based on its ijtihad, not necessarily adopt the conditions of the madhhab of the territory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و على السا بان الخلوة الصحيحة تقوم مقام الدخول في هذا ومثله الا في حل المبتوته فمبتوت الايلاج - وعلى السابع بان ذلك ليس من التلقيق الممنوع سواء سمياه تقليدا او تلفيقا كما يقتضيه كلام المجموع بادله وبياب النكاح عند قوله والمبنون حتى يونج بالغ الخر وهو الاولى بسماحة الدين والتوسعة على المسلمين دليس الانسان اذا قلد مذهبا من المذاهب يكون مربوطا به في جميع نواز له وكافة حوادثه ومسائله فهو خلان العقل والنقل ودين الله يسير و الله اعلم وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى اله وصحبه وسلم کتبہ بیده مستعجلا صالح التونسى المالكي المدرس بالمسجد النبوى يوم الاربعاء الرابع والعشرين من صفر الخير عام واحد وخمسين وثلاثمائة والت هجريه غفر الله لروعته . الاستفتاء مِنَ العُلَمَاءِ المَالِكيّة بالمرة الرابعة السوالات (۲) السوال الثانى ان جماعة المرفوع اليها اذا كانت حنفى المذهب ورفع اليها امر يوجب التفريق عند الحنفية ولا يوجب عند المالكية مثاله تقلبيل ابن الزوج إياها او غيره من الافعال التي توجب حرمة المصاهرة عند الاحنان فهل يجوز لهذه الجماعة الاحناف عند المالكية انا يحلموا با التفريق وهل ينفذ حكمهمان حكموا بها مع ان هذا الحكم ملفق خارق للاجماع ظاهر الان الحنفية ويعتبروا بحكم الجماعة. اى لم يعدوه بمنزلة حكم القاضي والمالكية وان عدوا جماعة المسلمين بمنزلة القاضى ولكن هذا الأمرك يوجب التفريق عندهم فهل يجوز مثل هذا التفريق اما بينوه مع نقل العبارات من كتب الفقه جزاكم الله تعالى عنا وعن سائر المسلمين - والذى فهمنا فى الجواب عن هذا السوال بناء على القواعد هو ان الفقهاء صرحوابان قضاء القاضي اذا صارت محلا مجتهدا فيه نفذ وهذا الحكم المسئول عنه مجتهدا فيه وهذه الجماعة تنوب مناب القاضي فاذا حكموا بالتفريق فقد تحقق ان الفضلا في فصلا مجتهدا فيه فينبغي ان ينفذ وكذا يقال في كل امر مجتهد فيه اياما كان اما لزوم محذور لتلفيق كما لزم في هذه الصورة حيث ان المحاكم حكم على المذهب المالكي و الحنفى والحكم حكم على المذهب الحنفي والمالكي فاعدل الا قاويل فيه أن التلفيق لا يجوز فى المسئلة الواحدة في مسئلتين او اكثر وهمنا كذلك لان كون الجماعة في حكم القاضي مسئلة وحرمة المصاهرة مسئلة اخرى فلا بأس بالتلفيق فيه هذا فهمنا وان كان صحيحا فيها و نعمت وان لم يصح فا وضوح النا وجه الغلط جزاكم الله تعالى و متعنا لكم الى از منة تتوالى - (۳) السوال الثالث الامر الذي يوجب التفريق بالاتفاق، ولكن كانت شرائطه مختلفا فيها مثلا اذا كان الجنون مطبقا فعند المالكية يرجل صاحبه سنة كماذا كان ذا اناقة واخذ ساداتنا الحنفية بقول محمد ان المجنون اذا كان مطبة الا يؤحل بل يفرق في الحمال كالجب فهل يحب على جماعة المسلمين أن يراعوا الشرائط المعتبرة عند المالكية اهم يجون الاكتفاء بالشرائط المرعية عند الحنفية افيضوا علينا متع الله الفتبين بطول بنائكم الفتوى من العلامة محمد بن على البيضاوى المالكى منع الله المقتبسين بعلومهم
And on the seventh: that valid seclusion takes the place of actual intercourse in this and similar cases, except in the matter of the irrevocable divorce (al-mubattata), for the irrevocable divorce requires actual penetration. And on the seventh: that this is not from prohibited talfiq, whether they call it taqlid or talfiq, as is indicated by the discourse of al-Majmu' with its proofs, and in the chapter of marriage at his statement: 'and the built upon...' until the end. And that is preferable for the tolerance of the religion and easing upon the Muslims. A person, when he follows a madhhab, is not bound by it in all his incidents and all his events and issues, that would be contrary to reason and transmission, and the religion of Allah is easy. And Allah knows best. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them peace. Written by his hand hastily, Salih al-Tunisi al-Maliki, teacher at the Prophet's Mosque, on Wednesday, 24 Safar al-Khair, year 1351 AH. May Allah forgive his lapse. The fatwa request from the Maliki scholars, the fourth time. Questions: (2) The second question: a council (jamā'a) is Hanafi in madhhab, and a matter is raised to it that compels separation according to Hanafis but not according to Malikis, for example, the kissing by the husband's son of her, or other actions that cause the prohibition of marriage by affinity (musahara) according to Hanafis. Is it permissible for this Hanafi council, according to Malikis, to rule for separation? And will their judgment be enforced if they so rule, despite this judgment being a talfiq that apparently violates consensus of the Hanafis? And they (the Maliki scholars) consider the judgment of the council as the judgment of a judge? Indeed, they (the Malikis) consider the council of Muslims as equivalent to a judge, but this matter does not compel separation according to them. So is such a separation permissible? Clarify for us with quotations from fiqh books. May Allah reward you on behalf of us and all Muslims. What we understood in answer to this question based on the rules is that the jurists have stated that when a judge's ruling is a matter of ijtihad, it is enforced. This ruling in question is a matter of ijtihad, and this council takes the place of the judge. So if they rule for separation, then it is established that it is a ruling in a matter of ijtihad, so it should be enforced. And likewise it is said for every matter of ijtihad. As for the objection of talfiq, as occurred in this scenario, where the scholar ruled according to the Maliki madhhab and the Hanafi, and the ruling was according to the Hanafi madhhab and Maliki, the strongest opinion therein is that talfiq is not permitted in one issue in two or more issues. And we meant similarly. Because the fact that the council is equivalent to a judge is one issue, and the prohibition of affinity (musahara) is another issue, so there is no harm in talfiq in this. This is our understanding. If it is correct, then it is fine; if not, explain to us the point of error. May Allah reward you and grant us benefit from you for successive times. (3) The third question: a matter that compels separation by agreement, but its conditions are different. For example, if insanity is continuous, then according to Malikis, one waits for a year for the male, as was the case? And our masters the Hanafis adopted the view of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) that if insanity is continuous, he is not given a reprieve, rather separation occurs immediately, like the leper. Is it incumbent on the council of Muslims to observe the conditions considered by the Malikis, or can they suffice with the conditions observed by the Hanafis? Enlighten us, may Allah grant the two fatwa-givers enjoyment with your long life. The fatwa from the scholar Muhammad ibn Ali al-Baydawi al-Maliki, may Allah benefit those who seek knowledge through them.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah presents a Maliki scholar's fatwa response and a subsequent set of questions from Maliki scholars regarding the practice of talfiq (legal patchworking) across madhhabs in divorce cases. The text begins by establishing that valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) stands in for actual intercourse in most rulings except for making a triple divorce irrevocable—a point of Hanafi law. It then asserts that such combinations of rulings from different madhhabs do not constitute prohibited talfiq, as the religion is meant to be easy. The main body consists of two fatwa questions: The second question concerns a Hanafi council ruling for separation based on grounds not recognized by Malikis (e.g., musahara through a stepson's kiss). The response argues that since the ruling is a matter of ijtihad, and the council acts as a judge, the ruling should be enforced. Talfiq is not an issue here because the council's authority and the grounds for separation are separate issues. The third question asks about continuous insanity: Malikis require a one-year wait before separation, while Hanafis (according to Imam Muhammad) separate immediately. The question is whether the council must follow Maliki conditions or Hanafi conditions. The passage ends with a request for clarification. The overall discussion is a practical application of the principles of taqlid, talfiq, and the authority of judicial councils in mixed-madhhab contexts.

Key Terms
تلفيق (talfiq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs to produce a new legal outcome not found in any single school.
خلوة صحيحة (khalwa sahiha): Valid seclusion between a married couple without intercourse that triggers most rules of consummation except for full irrevocable divorce.
مبتوتة (al-mubattata): A woman divorced with a final irrevocable divorce (talaq bain kubra), requiring actual intercourse for remarriage.
جماعة المسلمين (jamā'at al-muslimin): A council of Muslim scholars acting as a collective judge in the absence of a single qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the passage, why is the council's ruling for separation due to musahara not considered prohibited talfiq?
A) Because the council followed the Maliki school exclusively.
B) Because the ruling involves two separate issues: the council's authority and the grounds for separation.
C) Because talfiq is always permitted in divorce cases.
D) Because the Hanafi school does not recognise the concept of talfiq.

Key Takeaway
A council ruling in a matter of ijtihad is enforceable; talfiq is impermissible only within a single issue, not across multiple issues.

Talfiq in Independent Issues and Council's Authority as Qadi
Fatwa response on talfiq and qada by a Muslim community council

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a community council's judgment on a mujtahad fihi matter is binding, and distinguish when talfiq is permissible (independent issues) vs prohibited (single issue).

Core Idea
A Muslim council acting as qadi may issue binding rulings on mujtahad fihi matters; talfiq between independent issues is permissible.

This fatwa addresses a practical scenario: a council of Muslims rules on a marriage dissolution using both Hanafi and Maliki positions. The question is whether such talfiq is valid and whether the council's judgment is binding. The answer, rooted in Hanafi usul al-ifta, clarifies that the council stands in place of a qadi, so its ruling on a matter open to ijtihad is enforceable. Moreover, talfiq is not absolutely prohibited—it depends on whether the combined issues are independent or part of a single legal question.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two legal issues in the fatwa
Identify that the fatwa deals with: (1) whether the council's judgment is binding, and (2) whether talfiq between Hanafi and Maliki rulings is allowed. These are separate issues: the first is about authority, the second about consistency.
2
Define 'mujtahad fihi'
Understand that a mujtahad fihi matter is one where ijtihad is permissible because no definitive text settles it. The Hanafi principle holds that a qadi's judgment on such matters is final and cannot be overturned.
This contrasts with matters where the ruling is qat'i (definitive).
3
Extract the Hanafi rule on talfiq
From the text: talfiq is not allowed in a single issue, but if the issue comprises two independent sub-issues, it is allowed. Here, the council's authority is one issue, and the prohibition of affinity (marriage ban) is another, so talfiq is fine.
This is a key distinction for fatwa drafting.
4
Apply the principle to the scenario
The council's ruling on separation is binding because it is on a mujtahad fihi matter. The use of Maliki and Hanafi views on different sub-issues is permissible talfiq.
This resolves the initial dilemma.

Source Text

مثل هذا التفريق اما بينوه مع نقل العبارات من كتب الفقه جزاكم الله تعالى عنا وعن سائر المسلمين - والذى فهمنا فى الجواب عن هذا السوال بناء على القواعد هو ان الفقهاء صرحوا بان قضاء القاضي اذا صارت محلا مجتهدا فيه نفذ وهذا الحكم المسئول عنه مجتهدا فيه وهذه الجماعة تنوب مناب القاضي فاذا حكموا بالتفريق فقد تحقق ان الفضلا في فصلا مجتهدا فيه فينبغي ان ينفذ وكذا يقال في كل امر مجتهد فيه اياما كان اما لزوم محذور لتلفيق كما لزم في هذه الصورة حيث ان المحاكم حكم على المذهب المالكي و الحنفى والحكم حكم على المذهب الحنفي والمالكي فاعدل الاقاويل فيه أن التلفيق لا يجوز فى المسئلة الواحدة في مسئلتين او اكثر وهمنا كذلك لان كون الجماعة في حكم القاضي مسئلة وحرمة المصاهرة مسئلة اخرى فلا بأس بالتلفيق فيه هذا فهمنا وان كان صحيحا فيها و نعمت وان لم يصح فاوضحوا لنا وجه الغلط جزاكم الله تعالى و متعنا لكم الى از منة تتوالى
This separation [ruling] they have explained, with transmission of expressions from fiqh books, may Allah reward you on behalf of us and the rest of Muslims. And what we understood in answer to this question, based on the principles, is that the jurists stated that the judgment of a judge, when it becomes a subject of ijtihad, is enforceable. And this ruling asked about is a subject of ijtihad, and this group stands in place of the judge. So if they rule for separation, it has been realized that the matter was a subject of ijtihad, so it should be enforced. And similarly is said for every matter that is subject to ijtihad, whatever it may be. As for the occurrence of a problematic [element] due to talfiq, as occurred in this scenario where the courts ruled according to the Maliki and Hanafi [schools], and the rule [itself] was according to the Hanafi and Maliki [schools?], the strongest opinion therein is that talfiq is not permitted in a single issue in two matters or more. And our understanding is thus, because the fact that the group is in the position of a judge is one issue, and the prohibition of affinity is another issue, so there is no harm in talfiq therein. This is our understanding. If it is correct, then praise be to Allah; if not, then show us the error, may Allah reward you and grant us benefit from you for successive ages.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a fatwa response addressing two points: (1) the validity of a judgment issued by a group of Muslims acting as a qadi on a matter open to ijtihad, and (2) the permissibility of talfiq (piecing together rulings from different madhhabs) in certain circumstances. The author argues that since the group deputizes for a qadi, their judgment on a mujtahid fihi matter is binding. Regarding talfiq, he clarifies that if the issue comprises two independent sub-issues—here the authority of the group (one issue) and the prohibition of affinity (another)—then talfiq is permissible, unlike combining two schools within a single issue where it is prohibited. The response relies on the Hanafi principle that qada on ijtihadī matters is enforceable.

Key Terms
تلفيق (talfīq): Piecing together rulings from different madhhabs in a single case or fatwa.
مجتهد فيه (mujtahad fīh): A matter that is open to ijtihad, i.e., not settled by definitive evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the group is a qadi and can override normal rules.
B) Because the authority of the group and the prohibition of affinity are separate issues.
C) Because the Maliki and Hanafi schools agree on the ruling.
D) Because talfiq is always permissible in matters of marriage.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim council acting as a qadi may issue a binding ruling on a mujtahad fihi matter, and talfiq between independent legal issues is permissible.

Talfiq: Permissible Tool or Forbidden Following of Dispensations?
Critical refinement of talfiq and tattabu' rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on talfiq, identify its conditions, and distinguish it from tattabu' al-rukhas.

Core Idea
Talfiq is permissible but not in marriage; tattabu' al-rukhas is forbidden.

This passage addresses a critical distinction for the mufti: when is it legitimate to combine rulings from different madhhabs (talfiq) to solve a problem, and when does that cross into forbidden following of easy dispensations (tattabu' al-rukhas)? The context is a Hanafi judge wanting to apply a Maliki ruling on divorce. We will dissect the correct view, the conditions, and the caution required in family matters.

Guided Path
1
Define talfiq and tattabu' al-rukhas
From the passage, identify the core definitions: talfiq is combining rulings from multiple madhhabs in one case; tattabu' is following every easy dispensation without necessity.
The text explicitly contrasts the two concepts.
2
State the Hanafi position on talfiq
The correct view is permissibility, as affirmed by many later scholars including al-Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir. Note that some early scholars (al-Mazari, al-Ghazali) forbade it.
The tarjih (preferred view) is permissibility.
3
Identify the conditions and restrictions
From the passage: talfiq must not contradict consensus, combine contradictory rulings, or lead to tattabu'. Additionally, it is discouraged (and should be avoided) in matters of private parts (marriage, divorce) out of caution.
This is the key operational rule for the mufti.
4
Distinguish talfiq from tattabu' al-rukhas
Tattabu' is following every easy opinion without a valid reason or proper combination; it is unconditionally forbidden. Talfiq, when done with valid conditions, is a legitimate leeway.
Common error is conflating the two.
5
Apply to a case: the missing husband divorce
The passage gives the example of Hanafis wanting to rule with the Maliki position. This is valid talfiq if conditions are met, but caution is urged because it involves marriage.
The mufti must weigh necessity against caution.

The second issue: Know – may Allah guide me and you – that the Malikis do not see giving a ruling of separation between spouses because their madhhab is contrary to that, and they do not command the Hanafis to rule with separation because the matter in that is contrary to their madhhab. Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal mechanism of talfiq (combining rulings from different madhhabs to solve a problem) and the prohibition of tattabu' al-rukhas (following easy dispensations without necessity). The context is a Hanafi judge wanting to rule with a Maliki position on divorce of a missing husband's wife. The author clarifies that talfiq is permissible according to many scholars, but it is discouraged in matters of private parts (marriage, divorce) due to the need for caution. The passage also discusses the concept of transferring from one madhhab to another, citing multiple scholars: some permit, some forbid, and some differentiate. The key conditions for valid talfiq are: not contradicting consensus, not combining rulings that nullify each other, and not doing it for mere convenience or to evade clear obligations. This is a critical refinement of the rasm al-mufti methodology, showing that while talfiq is a leeway, its use is restricted especially in family law.

Key Terms
التلفيق (al-talfiq): Combination of rulings from different madhhabs in one issue; permissible but discouraged in marriage.
تتبع الرخص (tattabu' al-rukhas): Following every easy dispensation without necessity or proper combination; forbidden.
الفروج (al-furuj): Private parts; metaphorically includes matters of marriage, divorce, and sexual relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the established Hanafi position on the permissibility of talfiq?
A) It is absolutely forbidden
B) It is permissible according to the correct view but discouraged in marriage matters
C) It is permissible only for judges
D) It is permissible only in matters of worship

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is a permissible tool in fatwa when conditions are met, but it must be distinguished from the forbidden practice of tattabu' al-rukhas and avoided in marriage matters unless necessary.

The Mufti's Rule on Talfiq and Tattabu' al-Rukhs
Explains rule on talfiq and tattabu' al-rukhs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on talfiq, distinguish it from tattabu' al-rukhs, and identify the exceptions for marriage and the waswasi.

Core Idea
Talfiq is permissible if conditions are met, but tattabu' al-rukhs is prohibited except for the waswasi.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's work clarifies two critical concepts for the mufti: talfiq (combining rulings from different madhahib) and tattabu' al-rukhs (shopping for easy opinions). While talfiq is generally allowed in the Hanafi school, it comes with stringent conditions, especially avoiding contradiction of consensus. Pursuing dispensations, however, is strongly discouraged except for those afflicted with waswasa. The passage also addresses the situation when a Hanafi congregation follows a Maliki imam, emphasizing the need to observe all Maliki conditions to avoid tattabu' al-rukhs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key concepts
Read the opening definitions: talfiq is combining rulings from different madhahib in one issue; tattabu' al-rukhs is pursuing easy opinions from various madhahib without necessity.
Talfiq is not inherently prohibited; tattabu' al-rukhs is generally prohibited.
2
State the default rulings
According to the correct Hanafi view, talfiq is permissible (ja'iz) but tattabu' al-rukhs is prohibited (mamnu').
The passage says: 'الصحيح جواز التلفيق' and 'تتبع الرخص ممنوع'.
3
Analyze the conditions for valid talfiq
Three conditions from al-Zanati: (1) the combination must not violate consensus, (2) the person must believe in the virtue of the scholar followed, (3) the person must not be pursuing dispensations.
Example of violating consensus: marrying without wali, with mahr, and without witnesses – no single madhhab validates this combination.
4
Examine the exception for marriage
Even though talfiq is permissible, it should not be done in marriage (nikah) due to the need for caution in matters of lineage (furuj).
Al-Shaykh Hijazi recommends avoiding talfiq in private parts.
5
Determine the exception for the waswasi in tattabu' al-rukhs
Tattabu' al-rukhs is prohibited generally, but permitted for the muswas (person with obsessive doubts) to ease hardship.
This exception is mentioned in Nashr al-Nabdh and considered a good opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرها بما ينقض به حكم الحاكم من مخالف النص وعلى القياس وزاد في مراقي السعودى مخالفة الاجماع وقاعدة الدين والغيرة ان معناه رفع مشقة التكليف بابتاع كل سهل وفيه الينا منع التلفيق والذي قاله شيخنا الامير عن شيخه الصغير وغيره ان الصحيح جواز التلفيق وهر فسحة لكن لا ينبغي فعله في النكاح لانه يحتاط في الفروج مالك يحتاط في غيرها انتهى من بلغة السالك لاقرب المسالك للشيخ احمد الصاوى مع بعض زياده وبيان - و ما ذكره اعلاه من منع تتبع الرخص وكذا التلفيق نقله الشيخ محمد الامير فى مجموعة ثم تعقبه بقوله وسمعت من شيخنا عن شيخه الصغيرة وغيرها ان الصحيح جواز التلفيق وهو فسحة انتهى مع زيادة بيان قال محتى الشيخ حجازی ينبغي الا في الفروج للاحتياط فيها كما قاله بعض المحققين انتهى وذكر الشيخ حجازى ايضا قبل ان منع تتبع الرحمن نص عليه العراقي وغيره ثم ذكر منافشة الموانى فى سنى المهتدين في ذلك ولكن غير مسلمة وذكر الشيخ ابو العباس سیدی احمد بن عبد الرحمن الشهير باين حلولو في الضياء اللامع في شرح جمع الجوامع ان الانسان إذا التزم مذهبا معينا ثم اراد الخروج اختلف فيه فالماذري، والغزالي على عدم الجواز وصحح الرافعي الجواز والقول الثالث لا يجوز في بعض المسائل ويجوز في البعض والبعض الذى لا يجوز فيه هو الذي عمل به واختار عز الدين والقراقي في جواز الانتقال وان المذاهب كلها مسالك الى الجنة وذكر القراني عن الزناتي ان ذلك جائز بثلاثة شروط
الاول ان لا يجمع بينها على وجه يخالف الاجماع كمن تزوج
بغير ولي وله صداق ولا شهود فان هذه الصورة لم يقل بمجموعها احد
الثانى ان يعتقد فيمن يقلده الفضل باصول اخياره اليه . الثالث ان لا يتتبع رخص المذاهب انتهى - وجوز بعضهم تتبع الرخص للموسوس دون غيره كما في نشر النبود علی مراقي السعود وقال وهو قول حسن وامتناع تتبع الرخص شامل لمل توام مذهب معين وغيره انتقى منه تعلم من هذه النصوص أن تتبع الرخص ممنوع سواء التزم مذهبا معينا ام الا فى حق الموسوس والتلفيق يجوز على الصحيح غيرانه لا تليغي
فعله في النكاح والمسئلة التي ذكرتم من التلفيق لا من تتبع الرخص فتجوزوان كانت هنا في الفروج لانها عزيمة واحتياط واما ما نقله الشيخ حجازی عن بعض المحققين انه ينبغى الا في الفروج للاحتياط فيها فذلك .
في الرخصة انتهى والله اعلم
واما المسئلة الثالثة ذكر ثم فيها هل يجب على جماعة المسلمين العنفية ان يراعوا الشرائط المالكية ام بجوز الاكتفاء بالشرائط المراعيه عند الحنفية الى آخرة
اعلم وفتني الله واياكم انه يجب على جماعة المسلمين ان يراعوا شروط المالكية ليخرجوا من تتبع الرخص الممنوع لانهم اذا المرير اعواشه وطالمالكية فيكونوا اولا ارتكتبوا رخصة حكم جماعة المسلمين كما تقول المالكية والمحال انهم ليسوا المالكية ثم ارتكبط رخصة شروط الحنفية والحال انهم حكموا بمذهب المالكية
And branch it with what nullifies the judge's ruling from contradiction of the text and analogy; and he added in Maraqi al-Sa'd: contradiction of consensus, the foundation of religion, and the lesson that its meaning is removing the hardship of obligation by following every easy [opinion]. And in it to us is prohibition of talfiq. What our teacher al-Amir said from his teacher al-Saghir and others: that the correct [view] is permissibility of talfiq, and it is a concession, but it should not be done in marriage because one is cautious in [matters of] private parts just as one is cautious in other than them. End from Bulghat al-Salik li-Aqrab al-Masalik by Ahmad al-Sawi with some addition and clarification. And what he mentioned above of prohibition of pursuing dispensations and likewise talfiq, al-Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir narrated it in his collection, then he critiqued it saying: I heard from our teacher from his teacher al-Saghir and others that the correct [view] is permissibility of talfiq, and it is a concession. End with addition of clarification. Al-Shaykh Hijazi said: it should be [done] except in private parts for caution as some researchers said. End. And al-Shaykh Hijazi also mentioned before that the prohibition of pursuing dispensations was stated by al-Iraqi and others. Then he mentioned a discussion of the obstacles in Sani al-Muhtadin regarding that, but [it is] not accepted. And al-Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Sayyidi Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman, known as Ibn Halulu, mentioned in al-Diya' al-Lami' fi Sharh Jam' al-Jawami' that a person, if he commits to a specific madhhab then wants to leave, there is disagreement. Al-Mazari and al-Ghazali say impermissibility; al-Rafi'i declared permissibility; a third opinion says not permissible in some issues and permissible in others, and that in which it is not permissible is [the one] he acted upon. And Izz al-Din and al-Qarafi chose permissibility of transfer, and that all madhahib are paths to paradise. And al-Qarafi narrated from al-Zanati that it is permissible with three conditions: first, that he does not combine them in a manner contrary to consensus, like one who marries without a guardian, with [but] has a dower and no witnesses, for this scenario no one said [it is valid] in its entirety. Second, that he believes in the one he follows virtue in the principles of his choices. Third, that he does not pursue dispensations of the madhahib. End. And some permitted pursuing dispensations for the waswasi (one with OCD) but not others, as in Nashr al-Nabdh ala Maraqi al-Sa'd, and he said: it is a good opinion. And the prohibition of pursuing dispensations includes whether one commits to a specific madhhab or not. End. From this, you learn that pursuing dispensations is prohibited whether one has committed to a specific madhhab or not, except in the case of the waswasi. And talfiq is permissible according to the correct [view], however it is not fitting to do it in marriage. And the issue you mentioned is talfiq, not pursuing dispensations, so it is permissible even if it is in private parts because it is determination and caution. And as for what al-Shaykh al-Hijazi narrated from some researchers that it should be [avoided] except in private parts for caution, that is regarding dispensations. End. And Allah knows best. As for the third issue: mentioned there: is it obligatory for the Hanafi congregation to observe the Maliki conditions, or is it permissible to suffice with the conditions observed by the Hanafis? etc. Know, may Allah benefit me and you, that it is obligatory for the Hanafi congregation to observe the conditions of the Malikis to exit from the prohibited pursuit of dispensations, because if they [live] their lives and [adopt] the Maliki [madhab], then they would first have committed the dispensation of the ruling of the Hanafi congregation as the Malikis say, while they are not Malikis, then they commit the dispensation of the conditions of the Hanafis while they have judged by the Maliki madhhab.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the rules of talfiq (piecing together rulings from different madhahib) and tattabu' al-rukhs (pursuing dispensations). It opens by stating that a judge's ruling can be nullified by opposing clear text (nass) or analogy (qiyas), and adds opposition to consensus and the foundation of religion. The main subject is the prohibition of talfiq and tattabu' al-rukhs, but then it presents different scholarly views. Shaykh al-Amir reports from his teacher that the correct view is permissibility of talfiq, but it should not be used in marriage due to the need for caution in matters of lineage (furuj). Other scholars like al-Hijazi restrict this caution to marriage only. The passage then discusses the case of a person who commits to a specific madhhab and then wishes to leave it. It cites al-Mazari and al-Ghazali (impermissible), al-Rafi'i (permissible), and a third view distinguishing between issues acted upon and others. Al-Qarafi and Izz al-Din allow transfer between madhahib entirely. The three conditions for valid talfiq from al-Zanati are: (1) not combining elements that no single mujtahid has validated, e.g., marrying without wali, with mahr, and without witnesses; (2) believing in the virtue of the scholar followed; (3) not pursuing dispensations. Pursuing dispensations is generally prohibited except for a waswasi (person with obsessions). The final part addresses a practical question: if a Hanafi congregation follows a Maliki imam, they must observe all Maliki conditions to avoid tattabu' al-rukhs, because picking and choosing would constitute forbidden talfiq.

Key Terms
تتبع الرخص (tattabu' al-rukhs): اتباع رخص المذاهب المختلفة في المسألة الواحدة بقصد التسهيل دون ضرورة
التلفيق (al-talfiq): الجمع بين أقوال مذاهب متعددة في مسألة واحدة بحيث لا يخالف الإجماع
الموسوس (al-muswas): من يبتلى بالوسوسة في الدين فيجوز له تتبع الرخص للتخفيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on talfiq in marriage according to the correct Hanafi view?
A) It is absolutely permissible.
B) It is permissible but should not be done for caution.
C) It is absolutely prohibited.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is permissible with conditions; tattabu' al-rukhs is prohibited except for the waswasi; in marriage, talfiq should be avoided for caution.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Rules of Jamā'at Decision and Dispute Resolution
Supplement clarifying unanimity condition and dispute procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of unanimity for a Jamā'at's decision and apply the rule for overturning a prior decision based on its conformity to Shariah.

Core Idea
A Jamā'at decision must be unanimous; once given, it stands unless clearly contrary to Shariah.

This lesson unpacks two crucial procedural rules for the Jamā'at Muslimīn, the body of scholars overseeing the Hanafi-Maliki hila. The first rule insists on unanimity for validity; the second governs what happens when a party seeks to overturn a decision. These rules ensure both legitimacy and stability in the hila process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the First Addendum
Locate the passage under 'first addendum' which adds a note to the margin of the third point. It states that only a unanimous decision of the Jamā'at is valid. Understand that this was initially derived from principles and later confirmed by Maliki scholars.
This is a condition (shart) for the validity of the Jamā'at's ruling.
2
Analyze the Dispute Resolution Scenario
In the second addendum, follow the question: if parties disagree on which Jamā'at to approach, the Shariah claimant has the right to choose. If both are claimants, the first summons received decides jurisdiction; simultaneous summons require a lottery (qur'a).
The definition of mudda'ī (claimant) is key.
3
Determine the Rule for Overturning a Decision
If a Jamā'at has already decided, the other party may apply to another Jamā'at. The second Jamā'at can only overturn if the first decision is categorically against Shariah (qat'an khilaf al-shar'). If the decision aligns with any valid opinion, it cannot be overturned.
This protects valid ikhtilaf and prevents endless litigation.
4
Assess the Authority of These Rules
Note that the unanimity condition was written based on principles before Maliki confirmations arrived. Later responses from Allamah Salih al-Tunisi and Sheikh Abdullah al-Funi affirmed unanimity as a condition. The overturning rule is explicitly stated in the two answers to the istifta' in the fifth section.
The rules are not speculative; they are grounded in scholarly consensus.
5
Reflect on the Mufti's Application
As a mufti applying this rasm, you must ensure that any Jamā'at decision you accept or challenge meets the unanimity condition. When asked to overturn, you must first determine whether the prior decision clearly contradicts Shariah or is a valid ikhtilaf.
This is a practical test for any fatwa relying on a Jamā'at ruling.

والله سبحانه وتعالى اعلم
قاله و اذن بكتبه عبید ربہ محمد بن على البيضاوى غفر الله له یہاں تک جو فتاوئے مالکیہ لکھے گئے ہیں وہ سب پہلی طباعت
ضروری اطلاع
کے وقت حاصل ہو چکے تھے ، اور جن حضرات کی تصدیقات اس رسالہ کے ساتھ طلیع کی گئی اُن سب حضرات کی نظر سے گزر چکے ہیں ، اس کے بعد آٹھ صفحات کا ضمیمہ جس پر ھر سے حصہ تک لکھے ہوئے ہیں ، یہ فتاوی بعد حصول تصدیقات کے حاصل ہونے ہیں، اس لیے اطلاع دی گئی تاکہ تلبیس اختلاط نہ ہو فقط بسمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِلمة
بعد حمد و صلوة - معروض آنکه حیلہ ناجزہ شائع ہونے کے بعد اس کے متعلق چند علمائے کرام کی طرف سے کچھ اشکالات ہوئے تھے وہ مدینہ سورہ بھیج دیئے تھے وہاں سے جو جوابات آئے ہیں اُن کو بعینہ اصل عبارت عربی میں مجموعة الفتاوى المالكيه امذکورہ حیلہ ناجزہ کا تسمہ بنا کر مستقل شائع کیا جاتا ہے۔
چوں کہ اس تمہ میں دوامر ایسے ہیں جن کا اصل رسالہ اُردو میں اضافہ ضروری ہے۔ نیز ایک ضروری تنبیہ بھی خیال میں آئی لہذا ان کو بھی بطور ضمیمہ شائع کیا جاتا ہے حیلہ ناجزہ میں تحت عنوان تنبات ضرور یه متعلق جماعت مسلمین تنبیه اضافہ اول
کم دہ سوم جو کم درج ہے کہ جماعت مسلمین کا صرف وہ فیصلہ معتبر ہو گا
جو باتفاق الفراس پر حاشیہ ذیل کا اضافہ کیا جاتا ہے۔
عد اس وقت علمائے مالکیہ کا جواب اس مسئلہ کے متعلق موصول نہ ہوا تھا اس لیے قواعد سے حکم لکھ دیا تھا، بعد میں جواب آگئے ہیں اُن سے معلوم ہوا کہ سب علماء کا اس کہ پر اتفاق ہے کہ جماعت کا متفق ہونا شرط ہے کما صرح به العلامة صالح التونسى والشيخ عبد الله الفونى فى الجواب عن الاستفتاء بالمرة الخامسة.
عنوان بالا نہیہ سوم کے بالکل ختم پرین میں سوال وجواب ذیل کا اضافہ
اضافہ دوم کیا جاتا ہے۔ سوال : اگر مقدمہ پیش کرنے کی بابت فریقین میں اختلاف ہو، ایک فریق ایک جماعت کے پاس مقدمہ لے جانا چاہیے ، دوسرا فریق دوسری جماعت کے پاس تو کیس فریق کو ترجیح دی جاوے گی ، اور کس جماعت کو سماعت دعوی کا حق ہوگا اور اگر ایک جماعت فیصلہ کر چکے اس کے بعد دوسرا فریق کسی اور جماعت کے پاس اس فیصلہ کے خلاف درخواست دے تو دوسری جماعت کو سابق فیصلہ کے خلاف فیصلہ کرنا جائز ہے یا نہیں۔
الجواب : مقدمہ پیش کرنے کا اس کو حق ہے جواز روئے شریعیت مدعی قرار دیا جائے۔ دوسرے فریق کو اس میں اختلاف کا کوئی حق نہیں۔
ور اگر کوئی ایسا معاملہ ہو کر اس میں دونوں فریق شرعا مدعی تصویر کئے جاتے ہیں ، تو جس جگہ سے طلبی کا پیام پہلے پہنچ جائے دونوں کو اس کے ہاں جانا لازم ہے اور اگر دونوں جگہ سے علمی کا حکم ایک دم پہنچ گیا ہو تو پھر قرعہ ڈالا جائے جس کا نام قرعہ میں نکل آوے اُس کے ہاں مقدمہ پیش ہوگا ، اور جب ایک جماعت فیصلہ کر چکے ، اس کے بعد دوسرا فریق اُس کے خلاف درخواست دے تو اُس میں تفصیل ہے۔ اگر پہلا فیصلہ شرعیت کے قطعا خلیات ہے تب تو اس فیصلہ کے خامات صحیح فصار کیا جائے ۔ اور اگر وہ فیصلہ ایسا ہے جو قطعی طور پر تشریعیت کے خلاف نہیں بلکہ کسی نہ کسی قول کے موافق ہے تو اس فیصلہ کو توڑنا جائز نہیں گو دوسری جماعت کی تحقیق میں وہ صحیح نہ ہو كما هو المصرح في الجوابين عن الاستفتاء بالمرة الخامسة - والله اعلم اگر کسی جگہ حکومت کی طرف سے ایسا حاکم متعین ہو جس کا فیصلہ شرعا معتبر نہیں یعنی حاکم غیر مسلم ہویا احکام شرعیہ کی رعایت نہ کرتا ہو یا مذہب مالکیہ کے مطابق فیصلہ
And Allah Almighty knows best. He said and permitted its writing by the servant of his Lord, Muhammad ibn Ali al-Baydawi, may Allah forgive him. Up to here, whatever Maliki fatwas were written, all were obtained at the time of the first printing. Necessary notice: And the certifications of those gentlemen that were displayed with this treatise, all of those gentlemen have reviewed them. After that, an appendix of eight pages on which from 'هر' to 'حصہ' is written; these fatwas were obtained after obtaining the certifications. Therefore, notice is given so that there is no confusion or mixing. Only. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. After praise and salutations: The submission is that after Al-Hilatun Najizah was published, some objections were made by some virtuous scholars; they were sent to Madinah Sura; the answers that came from there, exactly in their original Arabic wording, under the title 'Majmu'at al-Fatawa al-Malikiyyah' of the mentioned Hilatun Najizah, will be published separately as a book. Since in this preface there are two matters that need to be added to the original treatise in Urdu. Also, a necessary warning came to mind, therefore these are also published as an appendix. In Al-Hilatun Najizah, under the title 'Tanbihat Daruriyyah' concerning the Jama'at Muslimin, first addendum: The note below is added to the margin of the third point, which states that only that decision of the Jama'at Muslimin will be valid which is by unanimous agreement. At that time, the answer of the Maliki scholars regarding this issue had not been received, so the ruling was written based on principles. Later, the answers came; from them it was learned that all scholars agree on this, that the agreement of the Jama'at is a condition, as explicitly stated by Allamah Salih al-Tunisi and Sheikh Abdullah al-Funi in the answer to the istifta' (inquiry) in the fifth section. Second addendum: At the very end of the above third point, the following question and answer is added. Question: If there is a dispute between the two parties regarding presenting the case; one party wants to take the case to one Jama'at, the other party to another, then which party will be given preference, and which Jama'at will have the right to hear the claim? And if one Jama'at has made a decision, and then the other party applies to another Jama'at against that decision, is it permissible for the second Jama'at to make a decision contrary to the previous decision or not? Answer: The right to present the case is for the one who, according to Shariah, is deemed the claimant. The other party has no right to dispute this. And if there is a case in which both parties are considered claimants according to Shariah, then the summons from whichever place reaches first, it is obligatory for both to go there. And if the summons from both places arrive at the same time, then lottery is cast; the one whose name comes out in the lottery, the case will be presented before him. And when one Jama'at has made a decision, and then the other party applies against it, there is detail in that. If the first decision is clearly contrary to Shariah, then that decision is overturned and a correct decision is made. And if that decision is not explicitly contrary to Shariah, but rather is in accordance with some opinion, then it is not permissible to break that decision, even if according to the research of the second Jama'at it is not correct, as is explicitly stated in the two answers to the istifta' in the fifth section. And Allah knows best. If in any place the government appoints such a ruler whose decision is not valid according to Shariah, i.e., the ruler is a non-Muslim, or does not observe the Shariah rulings, or makes decisions according to the Maliki school...
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is from the appendix of Al-Hilatun Najizah, clarifying two important procedural rules regarding the Jama'at Muslimin (the group of scholars set up to implement the hila). The first addendum establishes that the decision of a Jama'at is only valid if it is unanimous. This is a condition (shart) that was initially derived from principles (qawa'id) before the Maliki scholars' responses arrived, which later confirmed the unanimous agreement of all scholars on this point. The second addendum addresses a practical dispute: if the two parties cannot agree on which Jama'at to approach, the one who is the claimant (mudda'i) according to Shariah has the right to choose. If both are claimants (e.g., in a mutual claim), then the Jama'at whose summons reaches first takes jurisdiction; if simultaneous, a lottery (qur'a) is used. Once a decision is given, it can only be overturned if it is clearly and categorically against Shariah (qat'an khilaf al-shar'). If it is based on a permissible ikhtilaf (different scholarly opinion), it cannot be broken even if another Jama'at considers it incorrect. This ensures finality and stability of judgments within the framework of the hila. The passage also hints at a third issue: the ruler appointed by the government must be a Muslim and must observe Shariah; otherwise his decision is not valid. The Maliki school is mentioned as the basis for the hila, but the rules themselves are procedural.

Key Terms
جماعت مسلمین (Jamā'at Muslimīn): A group of Muslim scholars appointed to decide cases related to the legal stratagem (hila).
قرعہ (qur'a): Lottery used to decide which jamā'at hears the case when simultaneous summons occur.
مدعی (mudda'ī): The claimant in a case; the one with the right to initiate proceedings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second addendum, if one jamā'at has already given a decision and the other party applies to another jamā'at for a contrary ruling, what condition allows the second jamā'at to overturn the first decision?
A) If the first decision is clearly against Shariah
B) If the second jamā'at's research shows the first decision is incorrect
C) If the first decision was not unanimous
D) If the second jamā'at is of a different school

Key Takeaway
A Jamā'at's decision is valid only if unanimous, and once given, it stands unless it clearly contradicts Shariah.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced

Conditions for Community Adjudication: Parsing an Istifta'
A legal query parsing conditions for community judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal conditions for a Muslim community to act as a judge (qadi) in the absence of a ruler, and apply the Hanafi and Maliki perspectives on each condition.

Core Idea
The Muslim community can substitute for a ruler in adjudication only if conditions on procedure, agreement, delegation, and power are resolved.

This lesson examines a formal legal query (istifta') addressed to Maliki scholars about the rule that the Muslim community (jama'at al-muslimin) can act as judge when no ruler exists. The query raises six detailed questions covering procedure, collective adjudication, delegation, enforcement power, and conflict resolution. By parsing each question, we uncover the implied conditions and the cross-madhhab debate. This exercise sharpens your skill in breaking down complex fatwa inquiries and identifying the operative legal issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
Read the opening statement: the query says some Hanafis of India have accepted the Maliki view that jama'at al-muslimin stands in place of the ruler to resolve disputes (fasl al-khusumah). This is the central rule under scrutiny.
The phrase 'when there is no ruler in reality or meaning' hints at different levels of absence.
2
Pars Question 1: Procedure of community adjudication
The first question asks: does the entire community collectively hear and decide the case, or does it delegate to a single just scholar? Identify the two branches and the need for clarification.
This question directly affects how a mufti would guide the community in practice.
3
Pars Question 2: Conditions for collective judgment
If the community judges collectively, the query raises two sub-issues: (a) Malikis require a single judge – so how can collective judgment be valid? (b) Is agreement of the community required? The author notes that by analogy with private arbitration (tahkim), agreement is a condition according to both Hanafis and Malikis, but objectors say the analogy fails because the community's authority is general.
Note the use of qiyas and the objection to it – a key istidlal technique.
4
Pars Questions 3-5: Delegation, enforcement power, and the difference from a judge
Question 3: If the community delegates to one person, must he be from within that community? Question 4: Is overwhelming power (shoka) required for enforcement? Sub-question: under a non-Muslim government, can Muslims appoint a judge without obtaining power? Question 5: If power is not required for the community but is required for a judge, what is the distinction?
These questions reveal the practical challenges of community adjudication without state authority.
5
Pars Question 6: Conflict between community judgments
The final question (unfinished) presents a scenario: a woman raises her case to just neighbors who rule in her favor; the husband raises to another group that rules contrary. How is the conflict resolved?
The incomplete question underscores the need for a clear mechanism to prevent chaos.

Source Text

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الاستفتاء بالمرة الخامسة
الحمد لله وكفى وسلام على عباده الذين اصطفى اما بعد فالمعروض على ساداتنا العلماء المالكية انه قد اختار بعض احنات الهند ما صرح به المالكية من ان جماعة المسلمين تقوم مقام الحاكم في فصل المخصصات عند عدم الحاكم حا او معنى ولكن وردت على ذلك اسئلة تكتبها اليكم والمأمول من جنابكوان تشرفونا بالجواب عنها مع الدليل توجروا عند الله الجليل
الاول - اعنى ول الاسئلة قد صرحوا ان زوجة المفقود ومثلها ترفع امرها الى جماعة المسلمين عند عدم الحاكم لكن لم نجد في كتبهم كيفية قضاء الجماعة هل تلى تلك الجماعة بإجمعها سماع القضية وفصلها ام تقرض امرها الى عالم عدل يقضى فيها. الثاني وعلى الشق الاول اذا وليت الجماعة باجمعها شبهتات (الف) اذا ثبت عند المالكية ان تفرد القاضي في القضاء واجب والقضاء المشترك باطل فكيف يصح القضاء المشترك من الجماعة اليس هذا الحكم قضاء وان لم يكن قضاء فما ذا تشمونه رباء) هل يشترط اتفاق الجماعة على الحكوام لا وان لم يكن الاتفاق شرطا فكيف السبيل الى ترجيح رأى على رأى هل يرجح بالكثرة امر يمر عمر غيرها والذي نهنا ان الاتفاق على رأى شرط النفاذ الحكم من الجماعة وان لعد نجد هذا مصر حا لكن قناء على ما إذا حكم الخصمان رجلين اور جالا فالاتفاق على رأی واحد شرط كما صرح به ساداتنا الحنفية والمالكية معا الا ان بعض أهل العلم اور د على هذا القياس ان ولاية الحكمين مخصوصة بالمحكمين وولاية الجماعة عامة الجميع من رفع الامر اليها فافترقا افيدونا بالحكم الصحيح متعنا الله بطول بقائكم
الثالث وعلى الشق الثانى وهوان تقوض تلك الجماعة فصل الخصومة الى شخص واحد هل يجب ان يكون هو من افرادا الجماعة المرفوع اليها اولا يجوزان يكون من غير تلك الجمعة الرابع هل يشترط القاضي القوة القاهرة والشوكة الظاهرة على تنقيد الحكم املا. ويتفرع على هذا سوال اخر وهوان المسلمين اذا كانوا تحت حكومة غير مسلم ولم یکن ثمه قاض من جانب الحكومة فهل يصح نصب القاضى من عامة المسلمين مع ان القوة لا تحصل بمجرد تصبهم الخامس وان كانت القوة والشوكة شرطا للقاضي فهل تشترطا لقوة والشركة شرطا للقاضي فهل تشترط القوة والشوكة لتلك الجماعة التي رفع الامر اليهم فان قبل بصحة حكمها ونفاذه بدون القوة فما الفرق بين القاضى وتلك الجماعة بينوا بالدليل
السادس لو وقع الاختلاف بين جماعتين من المسلمين في فصل الخصومة فكيف يرجح احد الحكمين مثلا ادعت امرأة على زوجها التعنت ورفعت الامر الى عدول جيرانها واقامت البيئة على دعواها وفوق اولئك العدول بينهما ورفع زوجها هذا الامر الى جماعة أخرى من المسلمين واثبت نشوزها و حكمت هذه الجماعة خلاف ما حكم به اوليك العدول المذكورون سابقا نقد وقع اختلاف بين الحاكمين فكيف
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The fifth istifta'. Praise be to Allah and peace upon His chosen servants. To proceed: The submission to our masters the Maliki scholars is that some Hanafis of India have chosen what the Malikis have stated: that the Muslim community stands in the place of the ruler in resolving disputes when there is no ruler in reality or in meaning. However, questions have arisen regarding this, which I write to you. It is hoped from your excellency that you honor us with answers along with evidence, for which you will be rewarded by Allah the Exalted. First - meaning the first of the questions: They have stated that the wife of a missing person and the like raise her case to the Muslim community in the absence of a ruler, but we have not found in their books the procedure of the community's adjudication: Does the entire community collectively hear the case and decide it, or does it delegate the case to a just scholar who adjudicates? Second: Regarding the first branch, if the community collectively undertakes it, (a) if it is established with the Malikis that the singularity of the judge in adjudication is obligatory and collective adjudication is invalid, then how can the collective adjudication of the community be valid? Is this not a judgment? And if it is not a judgment, what do you call it? (b) Is the agreement of the community on the ruling required? And if agreement is not a condition, then what is the means to prefer one opinion over another? Is preference by majority? And what we have here is that agreement on one opinion is a condition for the enforcement of the judgment from the community, and we have not found this explicitly stated, but by analogy to when two litigants appoint two men or men, then agreement on one opinion is a condition, as stated by our masters the Hanafis and Malikis together. However, some scholars have objected to this analogy: that the authority of the two arbitrators is specific to the arbitrators, whereas the authority of the community is general for all who refer the matter to it. So they are distinct. Inform us of the correct ruling, may Allah benefit us with your long life. Third: Regarding the second branch, and that is when the community delegates the resolution of the dispute to a single person: Must he be from among the members of the community to whom the matter was raised, or is it permissible that he be from outside that community? Fourth: Is the judge required to have overwhelming power and apparent force to enforce the judgment or not? And branching from this is another question: If the Muslims are under a non-Muslim government and there is no judge from the government, is it valid to appoint a judge from the general Muslims, even though power is not obtained merely by their appointment? Fifth: And if power and force are conditions for the judge, are power and force conditions for that community to whom the matter is raised? If its judgment is accepted as valid and enforceable without power, then what is the difference between the judge and that community? Explain with evidence. Sixth: If a dispute occurs between two groups of Muslims in resolving a case, how is one of the two judgments to be preferred? For example, a woman claims hardship from her husband and raises the matter to just neighbors, and she establishes evidence for her claim, and those just ones adjudicate between them. Then the husband raises the matter to another group of Muslims and proves her nushuz, and this group judges contrary to what the aforementioned just ones previously judged. Now a difference has occurred between the two judges. How...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a formal legal query (istifta') addressed to Maliki scholars by a Hanafi who seeks clarification on the rule that the Muslim community (jama'at al-muslimin) can act as a judge in the absence of a ruler. The query presents six specific questions. First, the procedure: does the entire community hear the case collectively or delegate to a just scholar? Second, the issue of collective judgment: Malikis require a single judge, so how can a group adjudicate? The author notes that Hanafis and Malikis both require agreement of the judges in a private arbitration, but some object that arbitrators' authority is limited while the community's authority is general. Third, if the community delegates to one person, must that person be from the community? Fourth, is physical power necessary for enforcement? And a sub-question about appointing a judge under a non-Muslim government. Fifth, if power is required for a judge but not for the community, what is the difference? Sixth, how to resolve conflicting judgments from two different groups. The passage ends mid-sentence, continuing the sixth question. The author seeks clear evidence-based answers.

Key Terms
جماعة المسلمين (jama'at al-muslimin): The collective body of Muslims, which in this context is claimed to have the authority to adjudicate disputes in the absence of a ruler.
فصل الخصومة (fasl al-khusumah): The resolution or decision of a dispute between litigants.
القاضي (al-qadi): A judge appointed by the ruler with authority to enforce judgments, often requiring power (shoka).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the community's judgment to be valid, according to the analogy with private arbitration in the query?
A) The community must include at least ten members.
B) The community must have a single leader.
C) The community must agree on one opinion.
D) The community must be appointed by a ruler.

Key Takeaway
The Muslim community can substitute for a ruler in adjudication only if clear conditions on procedure, agreement, delegation, enforcement power, and conflict resolution are met, which this query reveals as critical gaps.

Ruling on Multiple Community Authorities in Marriage Disputes
Response to a query about the necessity of a single community authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fatwa hierarchy to determine the operative ruling when multiple community authorities exist in a town without a qadi.

Core Idea
A single formally appointed community is not required; practical necessity allows reliance on informal local leaders.

In this passage, Ashraf Ali Thanwi addresses a critical practical question: when no qadi is available, must a community be formally appointed, or can informal local leaders suffice? The author draws on Maliki fiqh and the realities of his time to refine the rule, showing how the Hanafi school accommodates necessity. By studying his reasoning, you will learn how fatwa hierarchy is applied in complex social contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Understand the problem: when a qadi is absent, who has authority to resolve marriage disputes? The initial claim requires a single community formally appointed by ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd.
2
State the Proposed Requirement
The questioner suggests that Muslims must rely on one community and cannot appoint multiple groups to avoid conflict.
This requirement seems impractical.
3
Analyze the Author's Rebuttal
The author gives two reasons: first, practicality (especially in India) prevents unity under one community; second, the Maliki position does not require formal appointment—a woman can raise her case to 'indefinite neighbors'.
The author cites the Maliki school as a valid precedent.
4
Apply the Fatwa Hierarchy
Determine the mufta bihi: the author's view that informal local leaders suffice becomes the operative ruling due to necessity and lack of a contrary explicit Hanafi text.
This demonstrates the principle of accepting a weaker opinion when needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السبيل إلى ترجيح حكم أحدهما على الأخران[؟] قبل في حل هذه السؤال أنه يجب على المسلمين الاكتفاء على نسب جماعة واحدة في بلدة واحدة ولا يجوز لهم نصب جماعات متعددة كيلا يكون الاختلاف الذي ذكر مساغا. قلنا أولا: إنه لا يمكن في زماننا هذا أن المسلمين لاسيما في الديار الهندية أن يجتمعوا على جماعة واحدة كما هو مشاهد. وثانيا: أن عبارة الفقهاء المالكية في هذا الباب رفعت الحمر[؟] إلى مدول[؟] جيرانها مطلقا، ولم يقولوا إنها رفعت الأمر إلى جماعة نصبها أهل الحل والعقد، فزيادة قيد النصب من أهل الحل والعقد زيادة على المنقول في المذهب على ما يظهر. والله أعلم، وعلمه أتم وأحكم.
The way to prefer the ruling of one over the other before in solving this question: that it is obligatory upon Muslims to rely on the lineage of a single community in one town, and they are not permitted to appoint multiple communities so that the mentioned difference does not become permissible. We said first: it is not possible in our time, especially in the Indian lands, for Muslims to unite under one community as is observed. Secondly, the statement of the Maliki jurists in this chapter is that she raises the matter to the indefinite neighbors, and they did not say that she raises the matter to a community appointed by the people of influence and contract. So adding the condition of appointment by the people of influence and contract is an addition beyond what is transmitted in the school, as it appears. And Allah knows best, and His knowledge is most complete and most wise.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) on the procedure when no qadi exists. The first author responds to a question: should Muslims rely on a single appointed community? The author argues that in their time (India), it is impractical to gather everyone under one community. Therefore, the Maliki position, which allows a woman to raise her matter to trusted neighbors without formal appointment, is accepted. This refines the rule: strict appointment by ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd is not required. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi acceptance of Maliki rulings in cases of necessity, reflecting the pragmatic approach of the later Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama'ah): A group of Muslims acting collectively in the absence of a qadi to resolve marriage disputes.
أهل الحل والعقد (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd): People of influence and contract who formally appoint authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author reject the requirement of a single formally appointed community for all Muslims?
A) Because Maliki scholars said it is not necessary.
B) Because it is impractical, especially in India, to unite all Muslims under one community.
C) Because the missing husband issue does not require a community.
D) Because the Hanafi school does not recognize community authority.

Key Takeaway
In the absence of a qadi, Muslims may rely on an informally recognized community, and formal appointment by ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd is not necessary.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

The Rule of Muslim Collective Judgment in Absence of a Qadi
Explaining the rule that a group of Muslims can judge like a qadi in his absence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rasm rule that a group of Muslims substitutes for a qadi in his absence, identify its furuat from the text, and apply the rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A group of Muslims collectively functions like a single qadi when he is absent.

This lesson examines a key principle for fatwa: when a formal qadi is unavailable, a collective of righteous Muslims can assume judicial authority, especially for family disputes. The passage from Asraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah clarifies the rule, its conditions, and its application to missing, absent, and impotent husbands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its trigger
The rule: 'A group of Muslims stands in place of the qadi when he is absent physically and effectively.' The trigger is the complete absence of a ruler or qadi.
2
Examine the group's functioning
The group must gather to hear and decide the case collectively. The text says 'the group collectively is like a single qadi.' Agreement is necessary.
Contrast with a single qadi who acts alone.
3
List the furuat (applied cases)
The text explicitly mentions: (1) wife of a missing husband (mafqūd), (2) wife of an absent husband (ghā’ib), (3) wife of an impotent husband (ʿannīn), and (4) a case of contempt or accusation. Each has specific procedures.
The four-year waiting period for the missing husband is a key detail.
4
Note the limitation (istithnā’)
If the husband is present but refuses to act, the group cannot intervene; the matter must go to a qadi. This is because the group's authority is premised on absence.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider a village with no qadi, where a woman’s husband has been missing for years. The local righteous elders investigate, set a waiting period, and if no news, allow her to remarry after iddah.
This is a direct application of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

I say: And with Allah is success, and in His hand is guidance to the straight path. The international [؟] issue: after a preamble from you at your statement: 'What is narrated from our masters up to his statement: to a just scholar who judges therein' - so its answer: [unclear] the people of the school mentioned that the wife of the missing person, the wife of the absent, the wife of the impotent, the man whose wife shows contempt or is accused of something, and the like – all of them raise their matter to a group of Muslims when the ruler is absent physically and meaningfully. And the appearance [؟] of the group to whom the matter is referred must necessarily gather hearing of the case and its final ruling. For the group collectively is like a single qadi, and there is no existence of the collective when some parts are missing. This is attested by the texts of the jurists where they said: 'Indeed, a group of Muslims stands in place of the qadi.' And the clearest in this chapter is what al-Qabisi and others from al-Qarawiyyin said: 'If a woman is in a place where there is no ruler, she refers her matter to righteous neighbors; they investigate his news fully, then set him an interval of four years, then she observes the waiting period of death and becomes lawful for husbands.' And likewise, the action of the group in the absence of an imam is like the ruling of an imam. Except and similar to it [؟] what Ahmad al-Sawi said on his statement: 'And maintenance is assessed from the property of the absent' i.e., the ruler stipulates it when the case is raised to him, or a group of Muslims if there is no ruler. When the husband's death is confirmed [؟] and he does not appear, the group pronounces divorce upon him following the earlier method. After the necessity of ijtihad by the ruler without specification if his [؟] is not known, or it is known and his absence is for ten days or more, and the messenger is close to him. If he appears, it is obvious; otherwise, divorce is pronounced upon him. [؟] in the waiting period [؟] to al-Hasan. Al-Sharnubi said: 'After that, they enable her to divorce herself and they rule by it, or they effect it.' End. As for their second statement: 'And on the first side, meaning when the group is appointed,' up to the statement: 'May Allah protect us through your long survival.' (Its answer): 'May Allah make us and you succeed to the straight path. The individuals of the group are not intended in this chapter; rather, what is intended here is their function, all of them or some of them, on the basis of communal obligation (fard kifaya), as a substitute for the imam and the qadi when they are absent. Therefore they said: 'Even one person, though there is a disagreement in that, unlike the qadi, because the missing person is a single entity and his ruling is not shared with others except in terms of widespread testimony. Do you not see that the testimony of all women: two of them in the chapter where men testify are like one man, and in the chapter where men do not testify, each one of them is like a complete man. And in the chapter of syntax, they considered the dual and plural as not singular. And in the chapter of subject and predicate, they considered them as singular. And from this is understood the validity of every ruling according to what its followers have established. And it is clear from this that the ruling of the group is not shared, but rather it is a ruling of a single individual in meaning, like the ruling of a qadi. And the two imams [؟] regarding judgment, as long as their ruling is judgment, and the police chief and the water official is likewise. And in al-Mudawwana: I said: 'Do you see that it is permissible for him to impose [؟] the owner of the police? Or is that only before a qadi or an amir appointed to judgment?' Malik said: 'I think the judgment of the people of these waterways is permissible.' Ibn al-Qasim said: 'They are only governors over those waterways, not qadis. I think that if the police chief sets a period for the impotent husband, it is permissible and that is valid.' And by this it is also known that everyone who judges as the qadi judges, whether by deputization or otherwise, his judgment is called judicial (qada).' As for your statement after (b) [؟] 'The agreement of the group on a ruling is stipulated' - its answer is that their agreement is obligatory and nothing else is possible because they are like a qadi.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage addresses the rasm rule that in the absence of a proper qadi, a group of Muslims (jamā'at al-Muslimīn) can collectively exercise judicial authority, particularly in matters like the case of a missing husband (mafqūd) or an impotent husband (ʿannīn). The author begins by responding to an objection: the claim that the matter must be referred to a just scholar who judges. The answer is that the Hanafi school (and others) have established that wives in such situations – e.g., of the missing, absent, impotent, or one whose husband defames her – may raise their case to a group of Muslims when the ruler is absent both physically and in effect. The group must gather to hear the case and deliver a ruling, functioning collectively like a single qadi. This is supported by clear texts from jurists like al-Qabisi and al-Qarawiyyin, who said that if a woman is in a place with no ruler, righteous neighbors should investigate her husband's status, set a four-year waiting period, then allow her to observe a death-waiting period and remarry. Similarly, Ahmad al-Sawi is quoted: maintenance for an absent husband is assessed by the ruler, or by a group of Muslims if no ruler exists. If the husband's death is confirmed or he does not appear after ijtihad by the group, they may divorce him. The passage further defends the concept by analogy: just as in testimony two women equal one man in certain cases, or in grammar the dual and plural are treated as singular in some rulings, so the group’s ruling is a unified ruling like that of a single qadi. Quoting from the Maliki Mudawwana, Malik ibn Anas allowed the judgment of 'people of waterways' (local governors) to stand, and Ibn al-Qasim clarified that their rulings are valid even if they are not formally appointed qadis. The conclusion: any judgment that meets the criteria of a qadi's judgment, whether by deputization or otherwise, is considered qada. Agreement among the group is necessary and inevitable because they collectively hold the authority of a qadi.

Key Terms
جماعة المسلمين (jamā‘at al-muslimīn): In this text, a group of upright Muslims (ideally three or more) who collectively exercise judicial authority in the absence of a ruler or qadi.
قاضي (qāḍī): A formally appointed judge with authority to settle disputes. In this passage, it contrasts with the substitute group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the absence of a qadi, a group of Muslims can collectively exercise judicial authority for family disputes, functioning as a single judge.

Reasoning Behind the Collective Judgment Rule: Analogy and Madhhab Dispute
Defending the rule through analogy and responding to objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the proof for the rule of collective judgment, including analogies from testimony and grammar, and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
The rule is supported by analogy to testimony and grammar, showing that a collective can function as a single entity.

This lesson delves into the reasoning behind the rasm rule that a group of Muslims substitutes for a qadi. The passage offers several lines of evidence: textual quotes from earlier jurists, analogies from the law of testimony and Arabic grammar, and references to Maliki practice. Understanding these proofs strengthens a mufti's ability to defend the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main dalil – textual quotes
The passage quotes al-Qabisi and al-Sawi directly on the missing and absent husband cases, establishing precedence.
2
Analyze the analogy with testimony
Two women witnesses equal one man in financial matters; thus a group can collectively equal one qadi.
The illa is the collective completion of a single legal function.
3
Analyze the grammar analogy
In Arabic, dual and plural can be treated as singular in subject-verb agreement, mirroring the group's unified legal standing.
This is a linguistic qiyas.
4
Consider the Maliki support
The Mudawwana quote shows that Malik allowed judgment of local governors even if not formally appointed qadis.
5
Evaluate the opposing view
The opponent insists on a single appointed qadi. The Hanafi response uses analogies and necessity to justify the group.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: hardship vs convenience.

Commentary
This passage addresses the rasm rule that in the absence of a proper qadi, a group of Muslims (jamā'at al-Muslimīn) can collectively exercise judicial authority, particularly in matters like the case of a missing husband (mafqūd) or an impotent husband (ʿannīn). The author begins by responding to an objection: the claim that the matter must be referred to a just scholar who judges. The answer is that the Hanafi school (and others) have established that wives in such situations – e.g., of the missing, absent, impotent, or one whose husband defames her – may raise their case to a group of Muslims when the ruler is absent both physically and in effect. The group must gather to hear the case and deliver a ruling, functioning collectively like a single qadi. This is supported by clear texts from jurists like al-Qabisi and al-Qarawiyyin, who said that if a woman is in a place with no ruler, righteous neighbors should investigate her husband's status, set a four-year waiting period, then allow her to observe a death-waiting period and remarry. Similarly, Ahmad al-Sawi is quoted: maintenance for an absent husband is assessed by the ruler, or by a group of Muslims if no ruler exists. If the husband's death is confirmed or he does not appear after ijtihad by the group, they may divorce him. The passage further defends the concept by analogy: just as in testimony two women equal one man in certain cases, or in grammar the dual and plural are treated as singular in some rulings, so the group’s ruling is a unified ruling like that of a single qadi. Quoting from the Maliki Mudawwana, Malik ibn Anas allowed the judgment of 'people of waterways' (local governors) to stand, and Ibn al-Qasim clarified that their rulings are valid even if they are not formally appointed qadis. The conclusion: any judgment that meets the criteria of a qadi's judgment, whether by deputization or otherwise, is considered qada. Agreement among the group is necessary and inevitable because they collectively hold the authority of a qadi.

قاضي (qāḍī): A formally appointed judge with authority to settle disputes. In this passage, it contrasts with the substitute group.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
