زوجہ مجنون کے فسخ نکاح کے احکام کا خلاصہ
سوالات : ما کیا مجنون کی بیوی کو شرعا یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ تفریق کا مطالبہ کرے اور مجنون کی زوجیت سے نکل جائے۔ اگر ہے تو اس کی کیا صورت ہے اور اس کے کیا شرائط ہیں؟ ا اور تفریق کے بعد مہر اور عدت کا کیا حکم ہے ؟
الجواب :- (1) جنون کی دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ نکاح کے وقت [جنون] موجود ہو اور بے خبری میں نکاح ہو جائے دوسری یہ کہ عقد کے وقت جنون نہ تھا مگر نکاح کے بعد لاحق ہو گیا خواہ ہمبستری سے پہلے ہوگیا ہو یا بعد میں ان دونوں صورتوں میں تفریق کا اختیار عورت کو ان شرائط کے ساتھ حاصل ہو جاتا ہے جو جواب [مذکور] میں ابھی آئی ہے مگر پہلی صورت یعنی نکاح کے وقت جنون کی صورت میں امام محمد رحمہ اللہ علیہ کے [نزدیک] بھی اختیار ہے اور مالکیہ کے نزدیک بھی اور دوسری صورت یعنی نکاح کے بعد جنون ہونے کی صورت میں صرف مالکیہ کے نزدیک اختیا[ر] ہو گا اس لیے دوسری صورت میں بغیر ضرورت شدیدہ کے نکاح فسخ نہ کیا جائے۔
(۲) تفریق فسخ نکاح کی صورت یہ
مجنون کی بیوی کے فسخ نکاح کا طریقہ [قاضی کی عدالت] ہے کہ
میں درخواست دے۔ اور شوہر کا خطر ناک مجنون ہونا ثابت کرے قاضی، واقعہ کی تحقیق کرے ، اگر واقعہ صحیح ثابت ہو تو مجنون کو علاج کے لیے ایک سال کی مہلت دے دے اگر سال گزرنے کے بعد [عورت] پھر قاضی سے درخواست کرے اور شوہر کا جنون اب تک موجود ہو تو عورت کو اختیار دے دیا جائے [اور] اگر عورت [اسی] مجلس میں فسخ نکاح کا مطالبہ کرے جس میں اس کو اختیار دیا گیا ہے تو قاضی تفریق کو واقع کر دے اور یہ تفریق اگر اس جنون کی وجہ سے کی گئی ہے جو کہ نکاح کے وقت موجود تھا تب تو طلاق نہیں، بلکہ فسخ ہے اور اگر نکاح کے بعد جنون ہو جانے کی وجہ سے تفریق کی گئی ہے تو اس [میں] طلاق ہونے کا احتمال ہے [لہذا] علماء مالکیہ سے تحقیق کی جائے اور جب تک تحقیق نہ ہو اس وقت تک طلاق قرار دینا چاہیئے کہ اس میں احتیاط ہے۔
زوجہ مجنون کے فسخ نکاح کی شرائط اور زوجہ مجنوں کو خیار فسخ حاصل ہونے کے لیے مندرجہ ذیل شرطیں ہیں اگر یہ شرطیں نہ پائی جائیں تو تفریق کا حق نہیں اس لیے ان کو غور سے سمجھ لینا لازم ہے ۔ (الف) ایک شرط یہ ہے کہ عورت کی طرف سے رضا مندی نہ پائی جائے، [یعنی] اگر نکاح سے پہلے جنون کا پتہ تھا اور اس کے باوجود نکاح کیا گیا تو خیار فسخ حاصل نہیں ہوتا اور اگر نکاح کے بعد جنون ہوا ہو تو یہ شرط ہے کہ جنون کی خبر ہونے کے بعد اس کے نکاح میں رہنے پر رضامندی ظاہر نہ کی ہو اگر ایک مرتبہ بھی رضا مندی ظاہر کر چکی تو خیار فسخ باطل ہو گیا ۔
(ب) دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ جنون کا پتہ لگنے کے بعد اپنے اختیار سے عورت
Summary of rulings on dissolution of marriage for the wife of an insane man. Questions: Does the wife of an insane man legally have the right to demand separation and leave his marriage? If so, what is the procedure and what are its conditions? And after separation, what is the ruling on mahr and iddah? Answer: (1) Insanity has two forms: one where insanity existed at the time of marriage and the marriage occurred unknowingly; the other where there was no insanity at the contract but it occurred after the marriage, whether before or after intercourse. In both cases, the wife gets the option of separation with the conditions mentioned in the answer. However, in the first case (insanity at marriage), Imam Muhammad also holds there is an option, and the Malikis also; in the second case (insanity after marriage), only the Malikis hold there is an option. Therefore, in the second case, the marriage should not be dissolved without severe necessity. (2) The procedure for dissolution: The wife of the insane man submits a request in the qadi's court, proves that the husband is dangerously insane. The qadi investigates; if the matter is proven, he grants a one-year respite for treatment. If after a year the wife again requests and the husband's insanity still exists, then the wife is given the option. If the wife demands dissolution in the same session where the option was given, the qadi effects the separation. If this separation is due to insanity existing at marriage, it is not divorce but annulment (faskh). If due to insanity occurring after marriage, there is probability it is divorce; thus inquire from Maliki scholars, and until inquiry, consider it divorce out of caution. Conditions for the wife to have the option of faskh: (a) The wife must not have consented. If she knew of the insanity before marriage and married anyway, she has no option. If insanity occurred after marriage, she must not have shown consent to remain in the marriage after learning of the insanity; if she consented once, the option is void. (b) Second condition: after learning of the insanity, of her own free will the woman [text incomplete].
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive summary of the Hanafi (and Maliki) rulings regarding a wife's right to seek dissolution of marriage due to her husband's insanity. It distinguishes two scenarios: insanity present at the time of marriage (pre-nuptial) and insanity occurring after marriage (post-nuptial). In the first scenario, according to Imam Muhammad (and the Malikis), the wife has the option of faskh (annulment). In the second scenario, only the Malikis grant the option; thus the author advises caution: without severe necessity, do not dissolve, and if dissolving, treat it as a divorce (talāq) out of caution. The procedure involves the qadi granting a one-year waiting period for treatment, after which the wife may demand dissolution. Conditions include that the wife did not knowingly consent to the marriage or to remaining after learning of the insanity. The passage also notes that if the insanity existed at marriage, the dissolution is faskh (not talāq); if later, it is considered talāq (with a need to verify with Maliki scholars).

Key Terms
فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikah): Annulment of marriage by judicial decree, different from talāq.
جنون (junūn): Insanity or severe mental disorder that makes the husband dangerous.
خیار فسخ (khiyār al-faskh): Right to annul the marriage due to a defect or condition.

The Third Party in Hurmat Musaharat: Witness, Not Defendant
Discusses procedural status of third party as witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a third party involved in establishing hurmat musaharat is considered a witness, not a defendant, and identify conditions under which his/her testimony is accepted.

Core Idea
The third party in hurmat musaharat is a witness, not a defendant; his testimony is accepted if he is upright and does not confess to disqualifying acts.

In cases of hurmat musaharat (prohibition due to relationship by marriage), a third party is often involved in the act that establishes the prohibition. This passage clarifies the procedural status of that person: he is not a defendant but a witness. Understanding this distinction is crucial for muftis when handling such cases, as it affects how testimony is solicited and evaluated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the third party's involvement raises the question of his procedural status in the case.
2
State the ruling
The third party is a witness, not a defendant. Therefore, he should not be compelled to testify as a defendant.
3
Identify conditions for acceptance
The testimony of the third party is accepted without doubt if he is upright (adil) and does not confess to any act that removes uprightness (e.g., zina).
4
Note the exception
If the third party confesses to a disqualifying act (like zina), there is hesitation; the mufti should research further with scholars.
This reflects Hanafi caution regarding self-incrimination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثبوت حرمت مصاہرت میں گواہ کی حیثیت

یہ تو ظاہر ہے کہ حرمت مصاہرت جن واقعات سے ثابت ہوتی ہے ان میں احد الزوجین کے ساتھ ایک اور کی بھی شرکت ہوتی ہے اور واقعہ کی صحت اور عام صحت و نیز شہوت کے وجود عدم کا اس کو بھی علم ہوتا ہے لیکن با دو دستی بسیار کہیں یہ جزئے نہیں ملا کہ مقدمہ میں اس سے بیان لیا جاوے گا یا نہیں اگر اس کا بیان ہو تو وہ کیا حیثیت رکھتا ہے لیکن قواعد میں غور و خوض کے بعد رجحان اس طرف ہوا ہے کہ وہ مدعا علیہ نہیں، اس واسطے اس کو مدعا علیہ بنا کر بیان پر مأمور نہ کیا جاوے بلکہ اس کو ایک شاہد سمجھا جائے، اور اس کی شہادت معتبر ہونے نہ ہونے میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص اپنے دوسرے افعال و اقوال کے اعتبار سے عادل ہو اور اس واقعہ میں بھی کسی ایسے فعل کا اقرار نہیں ہے جو مسقط عدالت ہو مثلاً ولی باتشبیہ وغیرہ کا بیان دے تو اس کی شہادت مقبول ہوگی کوئی شبہ نہیں، اور اگر کوئی ایسا فعل بیان کرے کہ جس سے اس کا نفسی ثابت ہوتا ہو تو اس کی شہادت معتبر ہوگی یا نہیں، اس میں بعض وجوہ سے تردد ہے بوقت ضرورت بمذہب و علماء سے تحقیقی کرلے جاوے۔
Status of witness in establishing prohibition due to relationship by marriage. It is obvious that among the events from which prohibition due to relationship by marriage is established, there is participation of another person along with one of the spouses. That person also knows the correctness of the event and also its public nature and existence or non-existence of lust. But in many cases, it is not determined whether his statement will be taken in the case or not; if his statement is taken, what status does it have? After deep consideration of the rules, the inclination is that he is not a defendant. Therefore, he should not be made a defendant and ordered to give a statement; rather, he should be considered a witness. And his testimony being acceptable or not is detailed: if that person is upright (adil) with respect to other actions and statements, and in this event also he does not confess to any act that would remove his uprightness (e.g., he gives a statement of 'like' etc.), then his testimony is accepted; there is no doubt. If he states an act that establishes his own wrongdoing (e.g., confession of zina), then there is hesitation whether his testimony will be considered or not. At time of need, research should be done with the respected madhhab and scholars.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage addresses a nuanced evidentiary question: when a third party (e.g., the mother-in-law who was touched) is involved in the act that establishes hurmat musaharat, what is his/her procedural status? The author reasons that this person is not a defendant because the primary claim is between the spouses. Thus, he/she cannot be compelled to testify as a defendant; rather, his/her statement is treated as testimony of a witness. The author then provides a rule: if the third party is known to be upright (adil) and does not confess to anything that would disqualify him/her (like zina), his/her testimony is accepted without hesitation. If he/she confesses to a disqualifying act, there is doubt about the acceptability of his/her testimony. The author advises that in necessary cases, one should research with the madhhab and scholars. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle of preserving the integrity of witnesses and avoiding self-incrimination in family matters.

Key Terms
عدالت (adalat): Uprightness of character required for accepting testimony.
مسقط عدالت (musqit adalat): An act that removes the quality of uprightness, making the witness rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is the testimony of the third party (e.g., the person who was touched) accepted without doubt?
A) If he confesses to a sin like zina.
B) If he is upright and does not confess to a disqualifying act.
C) If he is a relative of the wife.
D) If he testifies against the husband.

Key Takeaway
The third party in hurmat musaharat is treated as a witness, accepted if upright and not confessing a disqualifying act.

Witness Status in Establishing Hurmah Musaharat
Ruling on witness admissibility in hurmah musaharat cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on witness admissibility in cases of hurmah musaharat, distinguishing between types of contact and evaluating the testimony of an involved third party.

Core Idea
An involved person can testify if upright, but his testimony is questioned if he admits a disqualifying act.

This passage addresses a practical issue: when a third party participates in an act that may establish hurmah musaharat (prohibition of affinity), can that person serve as a witness? The text explains the conditions under which such testimony is accepted, and distinguishes between cases where desire is explicitly testified and where it is inferred. Understanding these details is crucial for a mufti when issuing fatwas on marital prohibition due to physical contact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the type of contact
First, determine whether the alleged contact is direct touching of private parts or kissing on head/forehead. The ruling on testimony differs because desire may not be inherent in the latter.
Touching the breast is considered direct, while kissing the forehead is not inherently indicative of desire.
2
Analyze the testimony regarding desire
If witnesses testify that the act occurred with desire, prohibition is established. If they only testify to the act without desire, the husband's oath is needed.
The presence of desire is key; without it, no prohibition arises.
3
Determine the status of a third party involved
The third party is not a defendant but a potential witness. Evaluate his integrity (adalah) and whether he admits any act that compromises his own credibility.
He is not automatically disqualified just because he participated.
4
Apply the ruling on admissibility
If the third party is upright and does not admit to a disqualifying act, his testimony is accepted. If he admits involvement that shows his own lack of integrity, there is hesitation.
The text notes that in cases of necessity, one should research the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھونے اور پستان چھونے کے دعوی میں تو صرف ان افعال کی شہادت دینے سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی شہوت کا انکار سموع نہ ہوگا اور تفریق کا حکم کر دینا لازم ہو کا اور پیشانی یا سر و غیرہ پر بوسہ دینے اور باقی بدن چھونے میں اگر یہ شہادت ہو کہ یہ افعال شہرت کے ساتھ ہوئے تھے اور اس کا علم قرائن سے شاہدین کو ہو سکتا ہے تو اس گواہی سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی ، در نہ صرف افعال پر شہادت دنیا کالعدم ہے اس کی بنا پر تفریق کا حکم نہ کیا جاوے گا بلکہ خاوند سے حلف لیا جاوے کہ یہ افعال شہرت سے نہیں تھے، اگر حلف کرنے تو خیر وریہ تفریق کا حکم کردیں گے۔

ثبوت حرمت مصاہرت میں گواہ کی حیثیت

یہ توظاہر ہے کہ حرمت مصاہرت جن واقعات سے ثابت ہوتی ہے ان میں [احد؟] الزوجین کے ساتھ ایک اور کی بھی شرکت ہوتی ہے اور واقعہ کی صحت اور عام صحت و نیز

..

شہرت کے وجود عدم کا اس کو بھی علم ہوتا ہے لیکن [با دو دستی بسیار؟] کہیں یہ جزیہ نہیں ملاکہ مقدمہ میں اس سے بیان لیا جاوے گا یا نہیں اگر اس کا بیان ہو تو وہ کیا حیثیت رکھتا ہے یکن قواعد میں غور و خوض کے بعد رجحان اس طرف ہوا ہے کہ وہ مدعا علیہ نہیں، اس واسطے اس کو مدعا علیہ بنا کر بیان پر معمور نہ کیا جا وے بلکہ اس کو ایک شاہ سمجھا جائے ، اور اس کی شہادت معتبر ہونے نہ ہونے ہیں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص اپنے دوسرے افعال و سے اقوال کے اعتبار سے عادل ہو اور اس واقعہ میں بھی کسی ایسے فعل کا اقرار نہیں ہے جو مسقط عدالت ہو مثلا [ولی با تشبیہ؟] وغیرہ کا بیان دے [انب؟] تو اس کی شہادت مقبول ہونے ہیں کوئی شبہ نہیں، اور اگر کوئی ایسا فعل بیان کرے کہ جس سے اس کا نفسی ثابت ہوتا ہو تو اس کی شہادت معتبر ہوگی یا نہیں ، اس میں بعض وجوہ سے تردد ہے بوقت ضرورت ب مذہب اور علماء سے تحقیقی کرلے جاوے۔
In the claim of touching and touching the breast, merely testifying to these actions establishes the prohibition of affinity; denial of desire is not heard, and a ruling of separation must be issued. And regarding kissing the forehead or head and other body parts, if testimony is given that these acts occurred with desire and the witnesses can know this through circumstantial evidence, then the prohibition of affinity is established by this testimony. However, testimony only on the actions is as if nonexistent; on its basis, a ruling of separation will not be issued. Rather, the husband will be asked to take an oath that these acts were not with desire. If he takes an oath, then fine; otherwise, a ruling of separation will be issued.

The status of a witness in establishing prohibition of affinity

It is apparent that in the events from which prohibition of affinity is established, another person also participates along with one of the spouses, and he also knows the validity of the event and the existence or absence of desire. But [unclear] it is not found that his statement will be taken in the case or not. If his statement is made, what status does it hold? After reflection on the rules, the inclination is that he is not the defendant, therefore he should not be made a defendant and his statement imposed. Rather, he should be considered a witness. And whether his testimony is credible or not, the detail is: if that person is upright (adil) in terms of his other actions and statements, and in this event he does not admit to any act that nullifies his integrity, such as [giving a statement like wali bi tashbih?], then his testimony is accepted without doubt. And if he mentions an act that establishes his own [involvement?], then there is hesitation on some grounds as to whether his testimony is credible. In times of necessity, one should research the school and scholars.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage explains the rules of testimony in cases where the prohibition of affinity (hurmah musaharat) is claimed due to physical contact. It distinguishes between types of contact: touching with desire vs. without. It also discusses the status of a third party who is also involved in the act. The text concludes that such a person is treated as a witness, not a defendant, and his testimony is evaluated based on his integrity. If he admits to an act that compromises his integrity, there is hesitation about accepting his testimony. This is a detailed ruling on the admissibility of evidence in such sensitive cases.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmah musaharat): Prohibition of marriage due to affinity (e.g., touching with desire creates in-law relations).
شہرت (shahwat): Sexual desire; presence of desire is necessary for establishing prohibition from touching.
شاہد (shahid): Witness; the third party is considered a witness, not a defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is rejected because he is a party to the case.
B) It is accepted without doubt.
C) It requires two witnesses to corroborate.
D) It is only accepted if he is a male.

Key Takeaway
An involved third party in a hurmah musaharat case is a witness, not a defendant; his testimony is accepted if upright and not self-implicating.

Guardianship in Marriage: Conditions and Authority
Ruling on marriage by guardians for minors with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions for a father/grandfather's marriage of a minor to be binding, and evaluate when a minor has the option of annulment (khiyar al-bulugh) after puberty.

Core Idea
Father's marriage with deficient conditions is invalid; other guardians' marriages give the minor the option of annulment.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Hila Najiza explains the Hanafi rules on marriage of minors by guardians. The key distinction is between the father/grandfather and other guardians. Understanding these conditions is essential for issuing fatwas in modern family law contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of guardians
The passage distinguishes between the father/grandfather (and son in some cases) and other guardians (like brother, uncle).
Father and grandfather have more authority.
2
Identify the two conditions for father/grandfather's marriage to be binding
The two conditions are: (1) the guardian was of sound mind at the time of marriage, and (2) he is not known for bad judgment (ma'ruf bi su' al-ikhtiyar).
If both conditions are met, the marriage is binding even if non-kufu or with ghabn fahish.
3
Understand the consequence when conditions are absent
If either condition is missing, the marriage is absolutely invalid (batil) when done with non-kufu or ghabn fahish.
Intoxication or known bad judgment invalidates the marriage.
4
Distinguish the rule for other guardians
For guardians other than father/grandfather, any marriage with non-kufu or ghabn fahish is absolutely invalid regardless of goodwill. If done with a suitable match, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor has khiyar al-bulugh.
Khiyar al-bulugh requires a qadi's decision to annul.
5
Recognize the role of khiyar al-bulugh and the need for qadi
Khiyar al-bulugh is the option upon puberty for a minor married by a non-authoritative guardian. Annulment requires a qadi's decree, or in absence, a shariah committee.
Without qadi, the marriage remains in effect until annulled by authority.

ہو جائے تو اس کا سب سے مقدیم ولی لڑکا ہے اور لڑکے کا کیا ہوا نکاح تمام احکام میں اُس نکاح کے برابر ہے جو کہ باپ نے کیا ہو مگر یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ نکاح کرنے کے وقت باپ کو غیر کفو ہونے نہ ہونے کا علم یہی حکم ہے اور اگر مقدار مہر معین کر کے کسی معین شخص سے اور نکاح پڑھانے کے لیے کسی کو وکیل بنا دیا ہے تب بھی یہی حکم ہے لیکن اگر کسی شخص کو مہر کی مقدار اور شوہر کی تعین کیے بدون بی وکیل بنا دیا کہ میں ہے اس کو خوب یاد رکھیں اکثر لوگ نا واقف ہیں۔ اور ان دونوں شرطوں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب اس نے نکاح کیا ہے اس وقت اس کی ظاہر حالت سے کم از کم خیر خواہی کی توقع ہو سکتی ہو۔ اور جب باپ نہ ہو تو وہ اولی تو نکاح بالکل ہی نہیں ہوتا خواہ اُس نے نہایت ہی خیر خواہی سے ایسا کیا ہو۔ اور اگر کفو کے ساتھ ہر شکل پر کیا ہو تو اس وقت نکاح صحیح تو ہو جاتا ہے ولیکن لازم نہیں ہوتا یعنی لڑکے لڑکی کو بالغ ہونے پر اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اس نکاح کو باقی رکھیں یا فسخ کرا لیں جس کی شرط بھی آتی ہے اور اختیار کو خیار بلوغ کہا جاتا ہے۔ اور خیار بلوغ میں نکاح فسخ ہونے کے لیے ہر ایک حالت میں قاضی کا فیصلہ شرط ہے قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بغیر کی حالت میں نکاح فسخ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور جس جگہ قاضی نہ ہو وہاں پر سلان حاکم با پنجائیت یعنی شرعی کمیٹی جس کی شرائط حیلہ نا جز جز دوم کے مقدمہ میں مذکور ہیں علی الترتیب فسخ کر سکتی ہے۔
...marries someone then that marriage becomes binding, meaning after puberty the girl does not have the right to annul it, whether the marriage was with a suitable match or not, and whether the proper dower was fixed or excessive deception was done in the dower. For a girl, excessive deception in dower is reducing her proper dower to an extent that is not normally tolerated, and for a boy it is setting the dower for the girl higher than her proper dower to an extent that is normally considered objectionable. But for a marriage with a non-suitable match or with excessive deception in dower to be valid, there are two conditions: First, that the person marrying was in sound senses at the time of marriage; if done while intoxicated, the marriage is absolutely invalid. Second, that he is not known for bad choice (ma'ruf bi su' al-ikhtiyar) meaning no such incident occurred before. If a child becomes insane, then the first guardian is the son, and the marriage contracted by the son is equivalent in all rulings to the marriage contracted by the father. But this ruling is when the father knew at the time of marriage whether it was with a non-suitable match. And if he married based on the husband's or his guardian's statement regarding suitability and later it proved non-suitable, its ruling is known under khiyar al-kafa'ah. And if the father or grandfather himself conducted the marriage, the same ruling applies; and if he appointed an agent specifying the dower amount and a specific person, the same ruling applies. But if he appointed an agent without specifying dower amount and husband, saying 'marry my daughter wherever', then that agent does not have the authority to marry with a non-suitable match or with excessive dower deception; if he does, it is invalid. The Shariah has given guardianship to many people in a specific order, details of which can be learned from fiqh books. On account of which it is generally thought that this person due to greed etc. does not consider benefit and consequence. So if a person is known for greed or imprudence, and he marries his minor son or daughter with a non-suitable match or with excessive dower deception, that marriage is absolutely invalid. And one who is insolent (fasiq muntahik) i.e. reckless and without honor, is also included in 'su' al-ikhtiyar'. Remember this well; many people are unaware. And the summary of these two conditions is that at the time he contracted the marriage, from his apparent state there could be at least expectation of goodwill. And when the father is not there, then the grandfather is the guardian, and the same detail applies to the grandfather as passed regarding the father: if the two mentioned conditions are found, then the marriage becomes binding, otherwise it is absolutely invalid. And after the grandfather, the brother etc. reach guardianship in this order, but they are not equal to the father and grandfather; rather their ruling is lower. That is, if someone other than father or grandfather, any other guardian, marries a minor boy or girl with a non-suitable match or fixes the dower with excessive deception, then the marriage does not take place at all, even if he did it with utmost goodwill. And if he did it with a suitable match in every respect, then the marriage is valid but not binding; i.e., the boy or girl upon reaching puberty has the choice to keep the marriage or annul it, and this choice is called khiyar al-bulugh. And for annulment in khiyar al-bulugh, the decision of a qadi is required in every case; without the qadi's decision the marriage cannot be annulled. And where there is no qadi, a ruling authority (sultan) or a council of five, i.e., a shariah committee (whose conditions are mentioned in the preface of Hila Najiza part two), can annul it in order.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rules regarding marriage of minors by their guardians. The author classifies guardians into two categories: the father and grandfather (and also a son in the case of a minor child?), and other guardians. The key ruling is that when the father or grandfather marries a minor ward (son or daughter) to a non-suitable match (ghayr kufu) or with excessive dower deception (ghabn fahish), the marriage is valid and binding upon the minor only if two conditions are met: first, the father/grandfather was of sound mind at the time (not intoxicated); second, he was not known as one who habitually makes bad choices (ma'ruf bi su' al-ikhtiyar). If these conditions are satisfied, the marriage is binding and the minor cannot annul it after puberty. If either condition is missing, the marriage is invalid ab initio. For other guardians (e.g., brother, uncle), the rule is stricter: if they marry a minor to a non-suitable match or with ghabn fahish, the marriage is absolutely invalid regardless of their goodwill. If they marry to a suitable match without deception, the marriage is valid but not binding; the minor has the option (khiyar al-bulugh) to either confirm or annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. This annulment requires a qadi's decree, or in the absence of a qadi, a shariah committee or equivalent authority. The passage emphasizes the importance of the guardian's capacity and trustworthiness.

Key Terms
کفو (kufu): Equality/suitability between spouses in lineage, religion, profession, etc.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Excessive discrepancy in dower (mahr) such that it is not normally tolerated
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of a minor upon reaching puberty to annul a marriage contracted by a guardian (other than father/grandfather) with a suitable match
ولی (wali): Guardian authorized to contract marriage for a minor
معروف بسوء الاختیار (ma'ruf bi su' al-ikhtiyar): Known for bad judgment or imprudence in dealings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a father who is known for bad judgment (ma'ruf bi su' al-ikhtiyar) marries his minor daughter to a non-suitable match, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is valid and binding, and the daughter has no option upon puberty.
B) The marriage is absolutely invalid (batil).
C) The marriage is valid but the daughter has khiyar al-bulugh.
D) The marriage is valid only if the father was intoxicated at the time.

Key Takeaway
The validity and binding nature of a minor's marriage depends on the type of guardian and whether specified conditions are met; father/grandfather have special authority, while other guardians' marriages give the minor an option upon puberty.

Conditions for Guardianship in Marriage of Minors
Explaining conditions for valid marriage by father, grandfather, and other guardians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid marriage contract by a guardian for a minor and distinguish between the rulings for father/grandfather and other guardians.

Core Idea
A father’s marriage for his minor child is binding only if he is trustworthy; otherwise it is void – other guardians’ marriages are void even with goodwill.

This passage from al-Hilat al-Najijah clarifies the conditions under which a guardian’s marriage of a minor is valid. The key distinction is between the father/grandfather, whose natural affection is presumed, and other guardians, whose authority is more limited. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mufti when advising on marriages involving minors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Types of Guardians
List the guardians mentioned: father, grandfather, and other guardians (brother, uncle, etc.). Note the hierarchy.
The passage groups father and grandfather together, and treats all others separately.
2
Extract Conditions for Father/Grandfather
For the father/grandfather, identify the conditions that make his marriage binding: he must not be known for greed, imprudence, or shamelessness; there must be at least an expectation of goodwill.
These conditions are about the guardian's character and apparent intent.
3
Determine Consequence When Conditions Fail
If the father/grandfather lacks these conditions and marries the minor to a non-compatible person or with a deficient mahr, the marriage is absolutely void.
'Absolutely void' (batil) means no legal effect.
4
Apply the Stricter Rule for Other Guardians
For any guardian other than father/grandfather, the marriage is void if he marries the minor to a non-compatible person or sets an excessive mahr, even if he appears to have goodwill.
Goodwill does not salvage the marriage in these cases.
5
Understand the Rationale
The difference is based on the degree of natural affection (shafaqa) presumed in the father and grandfather; other guardians are not granted the same leeway.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle of 'tasarrufat al-wali'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس کی بنا پر عموماً خیال ہو جاوے کہ یہ شخص معاملات میں لالچ وغیرہ کی وجہ سے مصلحت اور انجام بینی کو نظر نہیں رکھتا۔ پس اگر کوئی شخص لالچ یا ناعاقبت اندیشی کے سبب بنیاد میں مشہور و معروف ہو، وہ اگر نابالغ بیٹے یا بیٹی کا نکاح غیر کفو سے کر دے یا مہر میں عین نقصان کرے تو وہ نکاح بھی بالکل باطل ہے۔ اور جو فاسق منہتک یعنی بے باک اور بے غیرت ہو وہ بھی ساقط الاختیار کے علم میں ہے، اس کو خوب یاد رکھیں، اکثر لوگ ناواقف ہیں۔ اور ان دونوں شرطوں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب اس نے نکاح کیا ہے اس وقت اس کی ظاہر حالت سے کم از کم خیر خواہی کی توقع ہو سکتی ہو۔ اور جب باپ نہ ہو تو والی دادا ہوتا ہے، اور دادا جو نکاح کر دے اس میں بھی وہی تفصیل ہے جو باپ کے متعلق گزر چکی، یعنی مذکورہ دو شرطیں اگر پائی جائیں تب تو نکاح لازم ہو جاتا ہے، ورنہ بالکل باطل ہے۔ اور دادا کے بعد بھائی چا وغیرہ کو یہ ترتیب حتیٰ ولایت پہنچتا ہے، مگر وہ باپ دادا کے برابر نہیں بلکہ ان کا حکم ملاحظہ ہے، یعنی اگر باپ دادا کے سوا کوئی دوسرا ولی نابالغ لڑکے یا لڑکی کا غیر کفو میں نکاح کر دے یا مہر غیر فاحش کے ساتھ مقدر کر دے تب تو نکاح بالکل ہی نہیں ہوتا، خواہ اُس نے نہایت ہی خیر خواہی سے ایسا کیا ہو۔
Due to which it is generally thought that this person does not consider benefit and consequence in dealings because of greed etc. So if a person is well-known for greed or imprudence, if he marries his minor son or daughter to a non-compatible [person] or causes actual loss in the dowry, then that marriage is absolutely void. And whoever is a shameless transgressor, i.e., reckless and without honor, he is also in the knowledge of being stripped of authority; remember this well, many people are unaware. And the gist of both these conditions is that at the time he married, his apparent state [should be such that] at least goodwill can be expected. And when the father is not there, the guardian is the grandfather, and the same detail applies to the marriage done by the grandfather as passed regarding the father, meaning the two mentioned conditions—if they are found, then the marriage becomes binding, otherwise it is absolutely void. And after the grandfather, the brother etc. reach this order of guardianship, but they are not equal to the father and grandfather; rather their ruling is observant, meaning if someone other than the father and grandfather, another guardian, marries a minor boy or girl to a non-compatible [person] or fixes an exorbitant dowry, then the marriage does not occur at all, even if he did so with utmost goodwill.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from al-Hilat al-Najijah discusses the conditions under which a guardian's marriage of a minor is valid and binding. It states that a father who is known for greed or recklessness loses his authority to contract a binding marriage; his marriage is void if he marries the child to a non-compatible person or sets a deficient dowry. The same applies to a father who is openly sinful and shameless. For the marriage to be binding, there must be at least a semblance of goodwill. The same rules apply to the grandfather in the father's absence. However, for other guardians (like brothers), the ruling is stricter: even if they act with goodwill, a marriage to a non-compatible person or with excessive dowry is automatically void. This distinction is based on the degree of natural affection (shafaqa) assumed in the father and grandfather.

Key Terms
کفو (kufu): Compatibility in marriage; here specifically refers to social status, religiosity, and financial standing
خیر خواہی (khair khwahi): Goodwill or sincere concern for the minor's welfare

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a father who is known for greed marries his minor daughter to a non-compatible person?
A) The marriage is valid but the daughter has the option of puberty
B) The marriage is absolutely void
C) The marriage is valid if the mahr is fair
D) The marriage is suspended until the daughter consents

Key Takeaway
The binding nature of a guardian's marriage depends on the degree of presumed goodwill; father and grandfather have broader authority, others have none.

Categories of Non-Kufu Marriage in Hanafi Fiqh
Classification of non-kufu marriages into three legal types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three legal categories of marriage to a non-kufu husband and identify which scenario gives the wife a right to annulment (khiyar).

Core Idea
A non-kufu marriage may be void, valid binding, or valid with annulment – only the last requires qadi intervention.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najijah classifies marriages where the husband is not socially compatible. The author outlines three outcomes: void (batil), valid and binding (lazim), and valid but with an option to annul (khiyar). Understanding this classification is crucial for a mufti to advise women and qadis correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the opening lines of the passage to find the three legal effects mentioned: batil (void), sahih wa lazim (valid and binding), sahih wa ghayr lazim (valid but not binding, i.e., with khiyar).
The text states 'بعض میں نکاح باطل ہے اور بعض میں صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے اور بعض میں صحیح تو ہو جاتا ہے مگر لازم نہیں ہوتا'.
2
Understand the legal effect of each
For batil: the marriage is invalid from the start; no rights or obligations arise. For lazim: the marriage is fully valid and cannot be annulled. For ghayr lazim: the marriage is valid but the wife retains the option to seek annulment if she wishes.
The option of annulment (khiyar) is a distinctive feature of the third category.
3
Note the author's focus
The author explicitly states that the main purpose is to describe scenarios where the option of annulment exists, because only those require a qadi's judgment.
This indicates the practical importance of khiyar for judicial intervention.
4
Relate to the mufti's role
When a woman asks about her marriage to a non-kufu, the mufti must first determine which category the case falls into. If it is void, she must separate; if lazim, no annulment possible; if with khiyar, she may choose to annul or stay.
The classification directly guides fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غیر کفو میں نکاح ہونے کی کئی صورتیں ہیں بعض میں نکاح باطل ہے اور بعض میں صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے یعنی فتح کا اختیار بھی نہیں رہتا اور بعض میں مین تو ہو جاتا ہے مگر لازم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فسخ کا اختیار رہتا ہے۔ یہاں اصل مقصود تو انہی صورتوں کا بیان کرنا ہے جین میں خیار فتح ہو کیوں کہ قضائے قاضی کی ضرورت صرف انہی میں پڑتی ہے مگر ہم تمیم فائدہ کے لیے سب صورتیں درج کرتے ہیں اور ہر ایک ا جدا گانہ کم لکھتے ہیں جن کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔ پہلی صورت به که بالغ عورت بغیر اذن ولی عصبه غیر کفو میں نکاح بلا اجازت دلی نے غیر کفو می نکاح کرلے اس صورت میں خونی ں اس پر ہے کہ نکاح صحیح نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بالکل یا حل ہے حتی کہ اگر نکاح کے بعد ولی تقصیر جائز بھی رکھے تب بھی صحیح نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ نکاح سے قبل اجازت کا ہونا شرط ہے لہذا عورت و لازم ہے کہ ایسا ہرگز نہ کرے اگر کرے گی تو نکاح کالعدم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہمیشہ معیت میں مبتلا رہے گی۔ اسی سے اس صورت کا بھی حکم معلوم ہو گیا عورت کو غیر کفو ہونے کا علم نہ ہو جس میں عورت کو شوہر کے غیر کفر ہونے ا علم ہوا اور کفو ہونے کی شرط کرکے بابا شرط نکاح کیا ہوا دو عیدیں معلوم ہو جائے کہ رہا یہ کہ اگر قاضی نے اس کی در در بیانی پر دھوکہ کا انکار کردیا تو کیا کم ہوگا اس کی تحقیق اصل رسالہ میں خیار بلوغ کے ختم پر موجود ہے علماء کے ذریعہ سے معلوم ہوسکتی ہے نگاہ اور اگر عصبہ نہ ہونے کی حالت میں کسی اور کو ولایت نکاح پہنچتی ہو تو با منہ کو نکاح بغیر الکفر میں اس کے اذن کی حاجت نہیں
There are several scenarios of marriage to a non-kufu. In some, the marriage is void; in some, it is valid and binding, meaning that the option of annulment does not remain; and in some, it is valid but not binding, rather the option of annulment remains. Here the main purpose is to describe those scenarios in which the option of annulment exists, because the need for qadi’s judgment arises only in them. However, for completeness, we list all scenarios and write each one separately. Their detail is as follows: First scenario: That an adult woman marries a non-kufu without the permission of her 'asaba guardian. In this scenario, there are two [opinions?] that the marriage is not valid, rather it is absolutely void. Even if the guardian later validates it, it does not become valid, because permission before marriage is a condition. Therefore, the woman must never do this; if she does, due to the marriage being void, she will always remain in sin [or difficulty?]. From this, the ruling for the scenario where the woman is unaware of the non-kufu status is also known: [if] the woman knew the husband’s non-kufu status, and they stipulated compatibility and married on that condition, then two [opinions?] are known: that if the qadi rejected her [claim] of deceit, what would be the ruling? Its investigation is found at the end of khiyar al-bulugh in the original treatise; it can be known through scholars. And if in the absence of an 'asaba, guardianship goes to someone else, then for marriage to a non-kufu, his permission is not needed.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule that classifies marriages to a non-kufu (status-incompatible) husband into several categories. The author indicates that some such marriages are absolutely void (batil), some are valid and binding (lazim, no right of annulment), and some are valid but not binding (the wife retains the option to annul). The focus is on those giving the option, as they require qadi intervention. The first scenario described: an adult woman marries without her 'asaba guardian’s permission to a non-kufu. According to the Hanafi school, such a marriage is void ab initio; even the guardian’s subsequent consent cannot rectify it because consent must precede the contract. The woman is forbidden from doing this. Then the text mentions that the ruling for the case where the woman is ignorant of the non-kufu status is derived from the same principle. It also references a discussion from khiyar al-bulugh regarding the qadi’s acceptance of a claim of deceit. Finally, it states that if there is no 'asaba, the guardian is someone else (e.g., the sultan or a judge), and in such cases, that guardian’s permission is not needed for marriage to a non-kufu (likely meaning the marriage is valid without it). The OCR is very corrupt, but the main Hanafi positions are discernible.

Key Terms
غیر کفو (ghayr kufu): A husband who is not compatible in social status, lineage, wealth, or piety with the wife.
ولی عصبہ (wali 'asaba): A male guardian from the bride’s agnatic relatives (father, brother, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many categories of marriage to a non-kufu are there?
A) Two: void and valid
B) Three: void, valid binding, and valid with option to annul
C) Only one: void
D) Only one: valid with option

Key Takeaway
Non-kufu marriages are not all void; they fall into three distinct legal categories that determine the rights of the parties.

The Ruling on Non-Kufu Marriage Without Guardian Permission
First scenario: marriage to non-kufu without 'asaba permission – absolute void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that a marriage to a non-kufu without prior 'asaba guardian permission is void, and explain why later consent does not validate it.

Core Idea
Permission before contract is a condition; without it, the marriage is void ab initio and even later approval cannot cure it.

This passage details the first scenario in the classification: an adult woman marries a non-kufu without the permission of her 'asaba guardian. The ruling is unequivocal: the marriage is void (batil) from the start. Even if the guardian later gives consent, it remains invalid because the condition of prior permission was not met. The same principle applies when the woman is unaware of the incompatibility. The passage also touches on cases where there is no 'asaba, shifting guardianship to another authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and condition
The subject is an adult woman (baligh) and a husband who is non-kufu. The condition in question is the permission (idhn) of her 'asaba guardian. The text states that permission must be given before the marriage contract.
The phrase 'بغیر اذن ولی عصبه' clarifies that the guardian is the 'asaba (agnatic relative).
2
Apply the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, such a marriage is void (batil) – it is not merely invalid but has no legal effect whatsoever. The text even says 'بالکل یا حل ہے' (OCR corruption likely means 'bilkul batil').
This is the strongest form of invalidity.
3
Understand the reason: condition of prior permission
The passage explicitly says that permission before marriage is a condition (shart). Since the condition was not fulfilled, the contract is void. Later consent cannot rectify it because the condition must be present at the time of the contract.
This distinguishes it from the Shafi'i view where later consent can validate.
4
Note the consequence for the woman
The woman is forbidden to do this; if she does, she will be 'always in sin' (or difficulty). This indicates the gravity of the violation.
The phrase 'ہمیشہ معیت میں مبتلا' might be a corruption of 'ma'siyat' (sin) or 'mihnah' (hardship).
5
Consider the exception: absence of 'asaba
The passage ends with a statement that if there is no 'asaba, guardianship passes to someone else (e.g., qadi or sultan), and in that case, his permission is not needed for a non-kufu marriage. This suggests the marriage would be valid without that guardian's permission.
This is an important exception: the requirement of permission applies only when an 'asaba exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غیر کفو میں نکاح ہونے کی کئی صورتیں ہیں بعض میں نکاح باطل ہے اور بعض میں صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے یعنی فتح کا اختیار بھی نہیں رہتا اور بعض میں مین تو ہو جاتا ہے مگر لازم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فسخ کا اختیار رہتا ہے۔ یہاں اصل مقصود تو انہی صورتوں کا بیان کرنا ہے جین میں خیار فتح ہو کیوں کہ قضائے قاضی کی ضرورت صرف انہی میں پڑتی ہے مگر ہم تمیم فائدہ کے لیے سب صورتیں درج کرتے ہیں اور ہر ایک ا جدا گانہ کم لکھتے ہیں جن کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔ پہلی صورت به که بالغ عورت بغیر اذن ولی عصبه غیر کفو میں نکاح بلا اجازت دلی نے غیر کفو می نکاح کرلے اس صورت میں خونی ں اس پر ہے کہ نکاح صحیح نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بالکل یا حل ہے حتی کہ اگر نکاح کے بعد ولی تقصیر جائز بھی رکھے تب بھی صحیح نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ نکاح سے قبل اجازت کا ہونا شرط ہے لہذا عورت و لازم ہے کہ ایسا ہرگز نہ کرے اگر کرے گی تو نکاح کالعدم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہمیشہ معیت میں مبتلا رہے گی۔ اسی سے اس صورت کا بھی حکم معلوم ہو گیا عورت کو غیر کفو ہونے کا علم نہ ہو جس میں عورت کو شوہر کے غیر کفر ہونے ا علم ہوا اور کفو ہونے کی شرط کرکے بابا شرط نکاح کیا ہوا دو عیدیں معلوم ہو جائے کہ رہا یہ کہ اگر قاضی نے اس کی در در بیانی پر دھوکہ کا انکار کردیا تو کیا کم ہوگا اس کی تحقیق اصل رسالہ میں خیار بلوغ کے ختم پر موجود ہے علماء کے ذریعہ سے معلوم ہوسکتی ہے نگاہ اور اگر عصبہ نہ ہونے کی حالت میں کسی اور کو ولایت نکاح پہنچتی ہو تو با منہ کو نکاح بغیر الکفر میں اس کے اذن کی حاجت نہیں
There are several scenarios of marriage to a non-kufu. In some, the marriage is void; in some, it is valid and binding, meaning that the option of annulment does not remain; and in some, it is valid but not binding, rather the option of annulment remains. Therefore, the woman must never do this; if she does, due to the marriage being void, she will always remain in sin [or difficulty?]. Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule that classifies marriages to a non-kufu (status-incompatible) husband into several categories. The author indicates that some such marriages are absolutely void (batil), some are valid and binding (lazim, no right of annulment), and some are valid but not binding (the wife retains the option to annul). Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if an adult woman marries a non-kufu without her 'asaba guardian's permission, and the guardian later gives his consent?
A) The marriage becomes valid from the moment of consent
B) The marriage is void and remains void
C) The marriage is valid but the woman has the option to annul
D) The marriage is valid and binding

Key Takeaway
Prior permission of the 'asaba guardian is a condition for a valid non-kufu marriage; without it, the marriage is void and cannot be cured by later consent.

The Five Scenarios of Marriage with Non-Kufu: Rulings and Options
Lists five scenarios of marriage with non-kufu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five scenarios of marriage with non-kufu in Hanafi fiqh, apply the ruling of validity or annulment, and construct the khiyar al-faskh when applicable.

Core Idea
Marriage with a non-kufu is void unless the guardian permits; but with permission, it is valid and binding.

This lesson systematically presents five scenarios regarding marriage with a non-kufu (unsuitable match) in Hanafi family law. Understanding these scenarios is crucial for a mufti when asked about the validity of a marriage or the availability of the option to annul. The passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah clarifies when a marriage is void ab initio, when it is valid and binding with permission, and when the wife retains the khiyar al-faskh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five scenarios
List the five scenarios presented: (1) non-kufu discovered after marriage without permission, (2) marriage by non-father guardian or intoxicated father, (3) marriage by sober, non-corrupt father/grandfather, (4) adult woman marries with permission knowing non-kufu, (5) kafa'ah stipulated but non-kufu later discovered.
Scenarios 1 and 2 result in void marriage; 3 and 4 are valid and binding; 5 allows khiyar.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, state whether the marriage is valid (sahih), void (batil), or annullable via khiyar. Use the text's explicit rulings.
Distinguish between void ab initio (batil) and valid with option (sahih with khiyar).
3
Apply the distinction of virgin/non-virgin
Note how the option to annul (khiyar) and permission requirements differ based on whether the woman is virgin (bikr) or non-virgin (thayyib).
Silence suffices for virgin under father's guardianship; explicit consent needed for non-virgin or other guardians.
4
Analyze the role of guardian permission
Understand when guardian permission is required and how it affects validity. Permission from father/grandfather in scenario 3 makes marriage binding; lack of permission in scenario 1 makes it void.
Father/grandfather have binding authority (wilayah jabariyyah) for minors.
5
Apply the khiyar al-faskh
Identify when the option to annul is available (scenario 5) and how it is exercised: immediate verbal objection; silence invalidates the option for a virgin.
The option is lost if the woman delays or acts with consent (e.g., consummation).

وہ شخص کفر نہیں ہے تو عورت پر واجب ہے کہ معلوم ہوتے ہی اس سے الگ ہو جائے کیوں کہ قول مفتی بہ کے موافق غیر کفو سے بزن اذن ولی نکاح درست نہیں ہوتا تو جس وقت اس کا غیر کفو ہون ظاہر ہو گیا اس وقت ثابت ہوگیا کہ نکاح اول ہی سے باطل تھا۔

دوسری صورت یہ کہ باپ دادا کے سوا کسی دوسرے ولی نے نابالغ کا نکاح غیر کفو میں کردیا ہو یا باپ دادا نے کیا مگر وہ معروف بہ سوء الاختیار ہو یا نشہ کی حالت میں نکاح کیا ہو اس صورت میں بھی نکاح بالکل باطل ہے۔

تیسری صورت یہ کہ باپ دادا نے ہوش و حواس میں نکاح کیا ہو اور وہ باپ دادا فاسق مہتک نہ ہو، اور معروف بسوء الاختیار نہیں ہے اور یہ حکم عام ہے چاہے باپ دادا کو نکاح کے وقت کفو نہ ہونے کا علم ہو یا نہیں ہر ایک دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح نافذ اور لازم ہوجاتا ہے۔ البتہ اگر دوسری صورت یعنی اعظم ہونے کی صورت میں کفارت کی شروط پر نکاح کیا ہو تو اس کا حکم بلوارہ ہے جو کہ صورت میں آگے آرہا ہے۔

چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ بالغہ عورت کا نکاح ولی کی اجازت سے [کفو نہ ہونے کا علم ہوتے ہوئے] غیر کفو میں ہو تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ نکاح صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے اور کسی کو نکاح فسخ کرنے کا اختیار نہیں رہتا۔ یہ حکم تمام اولیا کے لیے عام ہے چاہے باپ دادا ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ کوئی دوسرا ولی ہو۔ لیکن فرق صرف یہ ہے کہ اگر لڑکی باکرہ ہے اور باپ دادا کی ولایت سے نکاح ہوا ہے تو اجازت کے لیے صرف لڑکی کا خاموش رہنا کافی ہوگا اور لڑکی [ثیبہ] (ہمبستری شده) سے یا باپ دادا کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے ولی کی ولایت میں نکاح ہوا ہے تو اجازت کی ضرورت ہے محض خاموش رہنا کافی نہیں۔

پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ بالغہ عورت کا نکاح ولی کی اجازت سے کسی ایسے شخص سے ہوا کہ جس کی کفاوت کا حال معلوم نہیں تھا لیکن نکاح کے وقت کفو کی شرط کر لی تھی یا واضح طور پر مشرط تو نہیں کی تھی لیکن شوہر کی طرف سے کفو ہونا ظاہر کیا گیا تھا اور اس پر اعتماد کر کے نکاح کر دیا ہو پھر ظاہر ہوا ہو ور ثابت ہوا ہو کہ کفو نہیں ہے اس صورت کا حکم یہ ہے کہ عورت کو بھی خیار فسخ حاصل ہوگا اور اس کے ولی کو بھی۔ لیکن اگر یہ عورت ابھی تک باکرہ ہو تو اس کا خیار خاموش رہنے سے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی اگر معلوم ہونے کے بعد فوراً کہہ دیا کہ مجھ کو اس شخص سے نکاح باقی رکھنا منظور نہیں تب تو اختیار باقی رہے گا اور بذریعہ حکم مسلم نکاح فسخ کر سکے گی، ورنہ اگر نامنظوری ظاہر کرنے میں کچھ بھی تاخیر کر دی تو خیار فسخ باقی نہیں رہے گا۔

یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب کہ لڑکی [ثیبہ] ہو اور اگر [باکرہ] ہو تو لڑکی کو اجازت ضروری ہے۔ بارہ [اور اگر گری نمیتہ ہوچکی ہے ہو لڑکی عاملاً شوہر کس و تعدیل کرے (یعنی بوسہ ہے یا چھوٹے) یا مہر اور ہفتہ ادا کر دے اور پیری اس کو چھوٹے یا بوسہ وغیرہ پر قدرت دستے یا مہر وغیرہ قبول کرنے کو یہ لالہ رضا مندی ہے اور جبر کا ہو کرنا اس وقت دلیلی رضا ہے جبکہ بالغ ہونے سے پہلے خلوت صحیحہ نہ ہو چکی ہوں]
If the person is not kufu, then it is obligatory on the woman that as soon as she knows, she should separate from him, because according to the mufta bih qawl, marriage with a non-kufu without the permission of the guardian is not valid. So when his non-kufu becomes apparent, it is established that the marriage was void from the beginning.

Second scenario: That a guardian other than father and grandfather married a minor to a non-kufu, or if the father and grandfather did so but they were known for bad choice or were intoxicated at the time of marriage - in this case the marriage is absolutely void.

Third scenario: That the father and grandfather married in a state of sobriety and they are not corrupt impudent persons, and are not known for bad choice. This ruling is general, whether the father and grandfather knew at the time of marriage that he was not kufu or not; in both cases the marriage is binding and effective. However, if in the second scenario (i.e., the case of 'azim - possibly meaning gross negligence) the marriage was contracted with conditions of kafa'ah, then its ruling will be discussed later.

Fourth scenario: That an adult woman's marriage is contracted with a non-kufu with the guardian's permission with knowledge of his non-kufu. The ruling is that the marriage is valid and binding, and no one has the option to annul it. This ruling is general for all guardians, whether father and grandfather or another guardian. But the only difference is that if the girl is a virgin and the marriage was under the guardianship of father or grandfather, then her silence suffices for permission; but if the girl is deflowered (non-virgin) or the marriage was under a guardian other than father and grandfather, then explicit permission is required, silence is not enough.

Fifth scenario: That an adult woman's marriage is contracted with the guardian's permission to a man whose kafa'ah status was unknown, but at the time of marriage she made kafa'ah a condition, or she did not explicitly stipulate but the husband was represented as kufu and she relied on that and married, then it becomes apparent and proven that he is not kufu. The ruling in this case is that both the woman and her guardian have the option to annul (khiyar al-faskh). But if the woman is still a virgin, her option is invalidated by silence. That is, if after discovering she immediately says she does not wish to remain married, then the option remains and she can annul the marriage through a Muslim judge; otherwise, if she delays expressing disapproval at all, the option to annul is lost.

This ruling is when the girl is a non-virgin. If she is a virgin, then permission is necessary. [...]
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage presents five legal scenarios regarding marriage with a non-kufu (unsuitable match) in Hanafi fiqh, focusing on the interplay between the guardian's authority and the woman's consent. 

The first scenario (partially visible) establishes that if a woman discovers her husband is not kufu, she must separate immediately because the marriage was void ab initio if performed without guardian's permission for a non-kufu. The second scenario covers marriages of minors by non-father/grandfather guardians or by intoxicated guardians—these are absolutely void. The third scenario states that a marriage by father/grandfather is binding even if they knew he was non-kufu, provided they are not corrupt. The fourth scenario gives an adult woman marrying with guardian's permission knowing he is non-kufu—the marriage is valid and irrevocable. The fifth scenario deals with when kafa'ah was stipulated or expected, giving an option to annul to both woman and guardian, but the virgin loses that option if she remains silent. The text also distinguishes between virgin and non-virgin women regarding permission requirements. The garbled final paragraph seems to discuss additional conditions for consent, possibly involving consummation or mahr. Overall, the passage systematically outlines the Hanafi position on kufu and the khiyar al-faskh, emphasizing the importance of guardian's role and the woman's knowledge.

Key Terms
کفو (kufu): Equality or suitability in lineage, religion, wealth, and profession between spouses.
خیار فسخ (khiyar al-faskh): Option to annul a marriage when one discovers that the spouse is not kufu as stipulated or expected.
ولی (wali): The legal guardian who has authority to contract a marriage. Hierarchy: father, grandfather, then others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fourth scenario, if an adult virgin marries a non-kufu with her father's permission and knowledge of the inequality, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is valid and binding, and her silence is enough for permission.
B) The marriage is void and must be annulled.
C) She has the option to annul the marriage for three days.
D) The marriage is suspended pending court approval.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the validity of marriage with a non-kufu hinges on the guardian's permission; without it, the marriage is void ab initio, but with knowledge and permission, it becomes binding unless kafa'ah was stipulated.

Iddah After Conversion: The Hanafi Tarjih Between Imam and Sahibayn
Details iddah rules upon conversion of one spouse with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy to resolve a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding iddah upon a wife's conversion in Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
When a wife converts in Dar al-Harb, iddah is disputed: Abu Hanifa says none, Sahibayn require three more menses.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute on iddah when one spouse embraces Islam. The ruling depends on location (Dar al-Islam vs Dar al-Harb) and which spouse converts. The author presents the consensus positions and then a critical ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples (the Sahibayn) on the wife's iddah in Dar al-Harb. Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of how Hanafi fatwa hierarchy operates—especially when precaution (ihtiyat) becomes the preferred path.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scenarios
Note the two location categories: Dar al-Islam (where presentation of Islam occurred) and Dar al-Harb (where it did not). Also which spouse converts.
2
Distinguish consensus vs ikhtilaf
In Dar al-Islam, iddah is wajib by consensus (ijma) regardless of which spouse converts. In Dar al-Harb, ikhtilaf arises only when the wife converts.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf: Imam vs Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifa rules no iddah because the marriage is already dissolved after three menses. The Sahibayn require an additional three menses as precaution.
The thamarah al-khilaf: immediate remarriage vs waiting.
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The author states precaution (ihtiyat) is to follow the Sahibayn, and notes that Imam Tahawi also chose this view.
This reflects the later Hanafi preference for the Sahibayn's position in mu'amalat.
5
Formulate the mufta bihi
The operative fatwa (mufta bihi) for a woman converting in Dar al-Harb after three menses: she must observe a fresh iddah of three menses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدت کا حکم ( بصورت اسلام احد الزوجین) اگر زوجہ اور شوہر دونوں دار الاسلام میں ہوں اور عرض اسلام کے بعد تفریق کی گئی ہے تب تو بالاتفاق عدت واجب ہے اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک یا دونوں دار الحرب میں ہیں اور اسی لیے عرض اسلام نہ ہو سکا بلکہ تین حیض گذر جانے کی وجہ سے بائنہ ہوئی ہے تو اس میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر شوہر مسلمان ہوا ہے تو بالاتفاق عدت واجب ہے نہیں اور اگر عورت مسلمان ہوئی ہے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک اس پر ان تین حیض کے علاوہ دوسرے تین حیض تک عدت گزارنا واجب ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک عدت واجب نہیں اور احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ صاحبین کے قول پر عمل کیا جائے حضرت امام طحاوی نے اسی کو اختیارہ فرمایا ہے ۔
Ruling of iddah (in the case of one of the spouses embracing Islam): If both the wife and husband are in Dar al-Islam and separation has occurred after the presentation of Islam, then by consensus iddah is obligatory. And if one or both of them are in Dar al-Harb, and for that reason the presentation of Islam could not occur, but rather she became bainah due to the passage of three menses, then in this there is detail: if the husband became Muslim, then by consensus iddah is obligatory; if the woman became Muslim, then according to the Sahibayn, upon her, in addition to these three menses, it is obligatory to observe iddah for another three menses, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, iddah is not obligatory. And precaution is to act upon the statement of the Sahibayn. Imam Tahawi has chosen this.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on iddah when one spouse converts to Islam. The author categorizes scenarios based on location (Dar al-Islam or Dar al-Harb) and which spouse converts. By consensus, if the husband converts and separation occurs, iddah is mandatory. If the wife converts, there is ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds no iddah, while the two disciples (Sahibayn) require three additional menses. The author recommends the precautionary view of the Sahibayn, endorsed by Imam Tahawi.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after dissolution of marriage before remarrying.
عرض اسلام (ard al-islam): The presentation of the invitation to Islam to the non-Muslim spouse before separation.
صاحبین (sahibayn): The two chief disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
بینونت (bainunah): The state of being irrevocably separated (bainunah kubra) due to passage of three menses in the context of a non-Muslim marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the Sahibayn require a woman to observe iddah after conversion?
A) When the husband converts in Dar al-Islam
B) When the wife converts in Dar al-Harb and three menses have passed
C) When both spouses convert together
D) In all cases of conversion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy prefers the Sahibayn's view requiring iddah when a wife converts in Dar al-Harb after separation due to three menses.

Three Positions on Wife's Apostasy: The Mufti's Rule on Zahir al-Riwayah
Explains three Hanafi rulings on marriage dissolution due to wife's apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi positions on wife's apostasy and apply the principle that fatwa is given on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
A wife's apostasy dissolves the marriage, but she must return to her original husband — that is the relied-upon position.

Many mistakenly think that a wife's apostasy frees her to marry anyone. This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi clarifies that the Hanafi school has multiple reports, but the operative fatwa requires her to re-enter Islam and remarry her first husband. Understanding the hierarchy of transmissions is crucial for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sayings (aqwal)
Read the passage and list the three distinct positions on the effect of wife's apostasy on marriage: (1) marriage dissolves but she must remarry same husband, (2) marriage does not dissolve, (3) she is enslaved in Dar al-Islam.
2
Distinguish authority levels
Classify each position by its transmission authority: Zahir al-Riwayah (most authoritative), fatwa of some mashayikh (less authoritative), and Nawadir (rare).
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary transmitted corpus of Imam Muhammad.
3
Apply the rasm al-mufti rule
Recognize that the mufta bihi (operative) position is the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling, as indicated by the author's emphasis and citation of major texts.
The rule: fatwa is given on Zahir al-Riwayah unless there is a compelling reason to adopt another.
4
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical consequence of each position: under Zahir al-Riwayah, the woman must remarry her original husband; under the second, she stays married; under the third, she becomes a slave.
The difference affects the legality of subsequent actions (e.g., second marriage).

تمام روایات فقیہ کے خلاف یہ تفریع کر بیٹھے (یعنی یہ مسئلہ نکالنے لگے کہ) اس نالائق کو تجدید سلام کے بعد دوسرے شوہر سے رہائی حاصل کرنے کا آسان علاج سمجھ لیا اور مرتد ہونے کی بلاء عظیم میں مبتلا ہو کر در محار و شامی میں اس کی تصریح ہے کہ ظاہر الروایہ جس میں فسخ نکاح کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ یہ بھی مذکور ہے کہ عورت تجدید نکاح کرے جیسا کہ قاضی خان اور عالمگیری اور در مختار و شامی میں اس کی تصریح ہے کہ ظاہر الروایہ جس میں فسخ نکاح کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ یہ بھی مذکورہ ہے کہ عورت کو تجدید اسلام اور شوہر اول سے تجدید نکاح پر بزور حکومت مجبور کیا جائے گا خواہ اس کے مرتد ہونے کی غرض خاوند اول سے علیحدہ ہونا ہی ہو یا حقیقہ[؟] یا اس کے عقائد بدل گئے ہوں دونوں صورتوں میں اس کو تجدید نکاح پر مجبور کیا جائے (کما صرح به الشامی)۔ اور بعض مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند اور بعض مشائخ بخارا المیل زاہد ابوالنصر لوسی اور ابوالقاسم سفار وغیرہم کا فتوی ہے کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونے کی صورت میں نکاح فسخ ہی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بدستور یہ عورت شوہر سابق کے نکاح میں رہتی ہے۔ تیسرا قول وہ نوادر کی روایت ہے امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ سے کہ یہ عورت دار الاسلام میں بھی کنیز بنا کر رکھی جائے گی اور اس کے خاوند کا قبضہ اس پر بدستور سابقت[؟] باقی رہے گا۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت مرتد ہو جائے تو اس کے نکاح کے بارے میں ابو حنیفہ کے تین قول ہوئے۔ ایک یہ کہ نکاح فسخ ہو جاتا ہے لیکن بعد تجدید اسلام اس کو تجدید نکاح پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اور کسی دوسری جگہ نکاح کرنے کا اختیار نہ دیا جائے گا ۔ (وهو ظاهر الروایة) دوسرا یہ کہ نکاح فسخ ہی نہ ہوگا بلکہ وہ دونوں بدستور زن و شوہر ہی رہیں گے۔ لیکن تفصیل اس مسئلہ کی یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں چلی جائے یا دار الحرب میں ہی مرتد ہو تو اس کو کنیز بنانے پر ظاہر الروایہ بھی متفق ہے تو اور اور ظاہر الروایہ کا اختلاف صرف اس میں ہے کہ دار اسلام میں رہتے ہوئے بھی کنیز بن سکتی ہے یا نہیں۔ لیکن اس روایت پر فتوی دینے کے ساتھ یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ تجدید اسلام اور تجدید نکاح سے قبل شوہر کو استمتاع و صحبت وغیرہ کی اجازت نہ دی جائے جیسا کہ متن میں بھی تحت عنوان "بعض مسائل بمرور" یہ عنقریب آتا ہے
Some people, due to not knowing the rulings [and] the legal ruling of the wife's apostasy, absolutely assumed that if a woman becomes an apostate (God forbid), the marriage will be dissolved immediately. And for that reason, due to lack of knowledge [؟], they made deductions against all transmissions of the jurist (i.e., they started deriving this ruling) that they considered this unworthy [woman] to have an easy cure to obtain release from the second husband after renewing Islam, and by falling into the great calamity of apostasy, they destroyed all the good deeds of their entire lives, while even their goal could not be achieved because in that case, marriage to another person is absolutely not permissible; rather, it is necessary that she re-enter Islam and remarry and stay with the first husband. So the following detail will be known. That detail is that regarding the case of a woman's apostasy, there are three sayings in the Hanafi school. One is Zahir al-Riwayah, whose summary is that from the woman's apostasy, the marriage is immediately dissolved, but then she will be imprisoned and forced to renew Islam and also forced to renew the marriage with her first husband, as is explicitly stated in Qadi Khan, Alamgiri, Durr Mukhtar, and Shami that in Zahir al-Riwayah, wherein the ruling of dissolution of marriage is given, along with it is also mentioned that the woman should renew the marriage. As is explicitly stated in Qadi Khan, Alamgiri, Durr Mukhtar, and Shami that in Zahir al-Riwayah, wherein the ruling of dissolution of marriage is given, along with it is also mentioned that the woman will be forced by government authority to renew Islam and renew marriage with the first husband, whether her purpose in apostasy is to separate from the first husband or actually [؟] or her beliefs have changed; in both cases she will be forced to renew marriage (as explicitly stated by al-Shami). And some mashayikh of Balkh and Samarkand and some mashayikh of Bukhara, such as al-Zahid Abu al-Nasr al-Lusi and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and others, issued a fatwa that in the case of a woman's apostasy, the marriage is not dissolved at all; rather, this woman remains in the marriage of the previous husband as before. The third saying is the narration of Nawadir from Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa that this woman, even in Dar al-Islam, will be kept as a slave, and her husband's possession over her will remain as before [؟]. The conclusion is that if a woman becomes an apostate, regarding her marriage, there are three sayings from Abu Hanifa. One is that the marriage is dissolved, but after renewing Islam she will be forced to renew marriage, and she will not be given permission to marry elsewhere (this is Zahir al-Riwayah). Second is that the marriage will not be dissolved; rather, both will remain husband and wife as before. But the detail of this issue is that if the woman goes to Dar al-Harb after apostasy or apostasizes in Dar al-Harb, then Zahir al-Riwayah also agrees on making her a slave; and the difference with Zahir al-Riwayah is only in whether she can be made a slave while staying in Dar al-Islam or not. But with giving fatwa on this narration, it is also necessary that before renewing Islam and renewing marriage, the husband should not be allowed intimacy and intercourse, etc., as will soon come in the text under the heading "Some issues gradually".
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage addresses a common misunderstanding about the legal effect of a wife's apostasy on her marriage. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, warns against the simplistic view that apostasy always dissolves the marriage and then the woman is free to marry another man. Instead, he presents the detailed Hanafi position on this issue. The passage is a ruling exposition with internal ikhtilaf. The author states that there are three reported positions (aqwal) from Imam Abu Hanifa. The first is the Zahir al-Riwayah position, which is the most authoritative. It states that the marriage is dissolved immediately upon apostasy, but the woman is then imprisoned and compelled to re-enter Islam and to renew her marriage contract with her original husband. This is done by force of the government if necessary. This applies whether her apostasy was motivated by a desire to leave her husband or due to a genuine change of belief. The second position, held by some mashayikh of Balkh, Samarkand, and Bukhara (such as Abu al-Nasr al-Lusi and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar), is that the marriage is not dissolved at all; it remains intact. The third position is a nawadir (rare) narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that even within Dar al-Islam, the apostate woman can be enslaved, and her husband retains ownership over her. The author then summarizes the three positions and notes a further detail: if the woman apostasizes and goes to Dar al-Harb, then even the Zahir al-Riwayah agrees on enslavement; the only disagreement is about enslavement within Dar al-Islam. Importantly, if one gives fatwa on the third position (enslavement in Dar al-Islam), it is still necessary that the husband is not allowed physical relations with her until she renews Islam and the marriage contract. This passage clarifies the mufti's rule: when multiple reports exist from the Imam, the fatwa is given on Zahir al-Riwayah unless there is a special reason to adopt another. The practical consequence is that a woman who apostasizes cannot simply marry someone else; she must return to her original husband.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; the most authoritative level of transmission in the Hanafi school.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less authentic transmissions from the founding Imams, not part of the six core books.
فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikah): Dissolution or annulment of marriage, as opposed to talaq (divorce by husband's pronouncement).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah in the Hanafi school, what happens to a woman's marriage when she apostasizes?
A) The marriage is dissolved and she may marry any Muslim man after renewing Islam.
B) The marriage is dissolved, but she is forced to renew Islam and remarry the same husband.
C) The marriage remains valid and she continues living with her husband as before.
D) She becomes a slave and her husband retains ownership over her.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa on a wife's apostasy is that marriage dissolves but she must remarry her original husband; this is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Khuruj an al-Madhhab: Necessity and the Mafqud Case
Author defends khuruj an al-madhhab under necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of khuruj an al-madhhab to determine when it is permissible to follow another school in cases of necessity, and evaluate objections based on contradictory narrations.

Core Idea
Necessity permits following another madhhab without deeming one's own weak.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's work addresses a critique on allowing a Hanafi woman with a missing husband to remarry by following the Maliki madhhab. The author defends the practice by clarifying that the Hanafi school is strong, but necessity (darura) can justify departing from it. He also counters an objection regarding Umar's alleged retraction, arguing the report is not authentic. This lesson will walk you through the key arguments and the mufti's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage defends the permissibility of following the Maliki madhhab in the case of a missing husband (mafqud) when the Hanafi ruling would cause severe hardship. Recognise that this is a dispute about the application of khuruj an al-madhhab.
The issue is not the strength of the Hanafi school, but whether necessity can override it.
2
State the Hanafi position on necessity
The author asserts that the Hanafi madhhab is strong and preponderant. However, necessity can permit khuruj an al-madhhab — adopting another school's ruling without considering one's own weak. This is a well-established principle in later Hanafi fatwa methodology.
Key phrase: 'ضرورت کی وجہ سے خروج عن المذہب کی گنجائش دی گئی ہے'.
3
Analyse the objection
The critic argues that following the Maliki ruling is invalid because Umar (ra) retracted his earlier statement that allowed remarriage after one year. Therefore, the Maliki position is based on a retracted opinion.
The objection hinges on the authenticity and acceptance of the retraction report.
4
Examine the author's response
The author responds that Imam Malik likely did not accept the retraction, just as Imam Ahmad rejected it. The report of retraction has not been found with a reliable chain; the dispute reduces to a difference in narration authentication. Since the chain is not proven, the objection is invalid.
The author cites a statement: 'He said: No, that the reports... lying from thirteen directions' — indicating multiple weaknesses.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that khuruj an al-madhhab is permissible under necessity, and the Maliki ruling can be followed in the mafqud case. The mufti must clarify that this is a concession, not a rejection of the Hanafi school.
This is consistent with the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy that permits following weaker opinions in exigencies.
